Records from Aftermath of Neukirchen Disaster in Germany 83

Deputy Chancellor Represents Government at Burial

▲ National News Agency, Neukirchen, 12th. The cleanup work after the disaster is nearing completion. According to current calculations, the death toll from this disaster has reached sixty-six, and one hundred and sixty people are injured, many of whom remain in the hospital in serious condition. It has been decided that the funeral for the deceased will be held on Tuesday. Deputy Chancellor von Papen will represent the government at the ceremony. Many condolence messages have been received from around the world, including from the President of France, British Foreign Secretary Simon, and Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss. The cause of the accident has not yet been definitively determined, but it is known that before the explosion, flames were seen emanating from the gas storage tanks.

▲ National News Agency, Neukirchen, 13th. The crisis from the explosion has passed, but the town of Neukirchen has been reduced to ashes, as if it had been subjected to hours of intense bombardment. As a result, people from southwestern Germany have been flocking to see the disaster area since yesterday, with over one hundred thousand visitors so far. Fifty-four bodies have been recovered and are still identifiable, including twenty-one gas plant workers, three other men (one of whom was an artist visiting on vacation), and twenty-one women, thirteen of whom were also employed at the gas plant. In addition, there were eight children. The remaining bodies have been burned beyond recognition.

▲ Reuters, Neukirchen, 13th. Today, families of the dead and missing went to the disaster site to find bodies in the rubble and mourn their homes. The scene was very tragic. Occasionally, when a woman found the body of her son or husband, she would rush forward, caress the body, and weep bitterly. If they found their child's usual toys, they would quickly pick them up, bringing tears to the eyes of those who witnessed it. At that time, the entire village was shrouded in a tragic atmosphere. The sounds of weeping were unforgettable. It has now been confirmed that a small explosion occurred at a benzol plant before the gas storage tank exploded. Some residents, alarmed by this, fled with their entire families, which saved many of the town's forty thousand residents. It is estimated that it will take at least a year to restore the town to its former appearance. It is reported that the victims will be buried tomorrow morning, at which time Deputy Chancellor von Papen will represent the government and the entire German people at the funeral. The federal government has declared Tuesday a day of mourning.

Overt Competition Between Japan and the US, Covert Struggles Between Japan and the Soviet Union (Japan News) 84

Military Preparations Compete with Each Other, Japanese-British Goodwill Gradually Decreases

Although Japan is wholeheartedly militaristic, it knows that three fists cannot beat four hands, and it knows the difficult situation it is currently in. If hegemony in the Pacific is not seized by Japan, then competition in the West Pacific, especially in the superior position in the Chinese market, will be difficult to maintain. Therefore, this year it will add one 10,000-ton submarine tender, two destroyers, and two 8,500-ton cruisers. In this way, Japan's naval power will increase again. The US Asiatic Fleet, with only one 10,000-ton cruiser as its flagship, will truly not be worth a strike.

Therefore, the United States of America is also trembling with fear, seeking a way to preserve itself. The first is to keep the Atlantic Fleet in the Pacific for the long term to guard against emergencies. This is not entirely intended to attack, but the significance of defending Honolulu outweighs other considerations. At the same time, the Senate Naval Committee proposed a naval shipbuilding plan until 1936], planning to build three aircraft carriers, nine cruisers, eighty-nine destroyers, and thirty-four submarines, totaling one hundred and thirty-five ships and 316,530 tons. In such a bad market, it is desperately trying to replenish warships. What is the purpose? Everyone knows it.

However, Japan has not reflected on this at all and has become even more violent. For example, its invasion of Manchuria, not to mention foreigners, even knowledgeable people in Japan, from the Communist Party to the liberals, have expressed their full dissatisfaction. However, the warlords are still desperately stubborn, wanting to expand the chaos to Jehol, extend it to Tianjin, and even spread it to Shandong. In short, they want to monopolize the Chinese market. Therefore, even Britain, which has always been pro-Japanese [formerly an ally of Japan], feels that Japan is too domineering and unreasonable [not only wants to swallow "Manchuria" whole, but also has the preparation and intention to squeeze other forces out of North China]. Therefore, British goodwill towards Japan seems to be gradually decreasing, and the League of Nations also has a tendency to restrain Japan.

On the other hand, the Soviet Union, which is in an adversarial position with Japan on land and is also the enemy that Japan uses as an excuse, has a cold and indifferent eye towards the Northeast issue and Japan's attack on North China and annexation of Manchuria, observing quietly from the sidelines. However, its military preparations are very sufficient, and Japan is indeed somewhat wary of it. Therefore, one part of Japan's new plan to strengthen national defense this year also imitates the Soviet Union's intention to train mechanized troops. However, it did not set up mechanized troop divisions like the Soviet Union. It only expanded the 1st Tank Company attached to the 12th Division into a tank regiment, and at the same time expanded the tank team of the Chiba Army Engineering School into a regiment. The expansion cost for these two regiments this year alone is 11 million yen, which will probably be completed by June. At the same time, the 19th Division was mobilized to North Manchuria for security, adding a current cancerous tumor.

Since the conflict between Japan and the Soviet Union is becoming increasingly acute, things are also very coincidental. In January of this year, four Soviet whaling ships sailed from the Indian Ocean, originally intending to engage in whaling in the Sea of Okhotsk (among them, the Arius was an old 5,000-ton ship, serving as a mother ship, and the other three were each 260 tons, recently assembled in Norway). For some reason, they mistakenly entered the military fortress area of Futami Port on the Ogasawara Islands. As a result, the red fishing boats were arrested.

Initially, according to the opinion of the Tokyo District Court, they were to be charged with military espionage for spying on the fortress (measuring the depth of the harbor and surveying the situation). Later, the Ministry of Justice thought this was very inappropriate, so it dropped the military espionage charge. However, [Futami Port] is not a commercial port, so they were charged with violating the Shipping Act. Originally, they intended to confiscate the three whaling ships, but after consultations between the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Justice, they believed that if they really confiscated the ships, their value would only be one million yen, and the diplomatic relations between Japan and the Soviet Union would be further strained. Therefore, they stopped confiscating the ships and used the following charges:

(1) The Ogasawara Islands are a "non-opening port." The Arius should not have led the other three ships to call for supplies of drinking water and coal.

(2) The captain of the ship should have known that the area was a fortress area and should not have entered it arbitrarily.

(3) Even if measuring the water depth could be excused for navigational safety, violating the Shipping Act was very serious.

Therefore, the three captains were each fined 1,500 yen, and the storm came to an end. However, the rift between Japan and the Soviet Union and the opposition between Japan and the United States became more and more serious. (February 9)

Northern Anhui Lieshan Coal Mine Returns to Commercial Shares 87

Official Share Management Suffers Heavy Losses

Commercial Shares Submit Request to Ministry to Take Over Responsibility

Bengbu Correspondence. The Lieshan Coal Mine in Su County is the most famous mine in Anhui Province, with a very rich annual output. The fuel for Jiangsu, Anhui, and Henan provinces is mostly supplied by it. The mine was initially opened by local gentry and was originally named Puyi Coal Mine Company. Later, it was seized by Ni Sichong, who added shares and expanded it, gradually developing it. By the ninth year of the Republic, business had been expanded again, raising a total of 1.5 million yuan in shares. In the sixteenth year of the Republic, the National Revolutionary Army's Northern Expedition recovered Jiangsu and Anhui. The authorities found that Ni had 600,000 yuan of shares in the mine, which was deemed to be the property of a rebel. The Ministry of Agriculture and Mining sent personnel to take over and changed the company to Lieshan Coal Mine Bureau, which was run by the government. However, due to the military situation at the time, all matters at the mine were suspended, and mining could not continue. The Ministry of Agriculture and Mining suffered heavy annual losses, and the mining business showed no signs of improvement. In the seventeenth year, non-Ni shareholders jointly petitioned the National Government to return the original mine to restore property rights. After repeated negotiations, in the eighteenth year, the Lieshan Coal Mine Bureau was abolished and changed to the Lieshan Coal Mine Co., Ltd., a joint venture between the government and commercial interests. Ni's 600,000 yuan of shares remained state-owned, while commercial shares accounted for 900,000 yuan, with a total of 1.5 million yuan in shares. After the mine was changed to a joint venture, the Ministry of Industry designated six directors each for the government and commercial shares to form a board of directors in Beijing. The board of directors would elect a general manager and an assistant manager, who would be appointed by the Ministry of Industry. However, in practice, the directors of the government shares were responsible. In recent years, due to poor management, the company has suffered considerable losses. All commercial share dividends for several years have not been paid out. General Manager Huang Jintao found it difficult to cope and felt that handling affairs was tricky, so he requested to resign. The directors of the commercial shares, considering the company's annual losses, feared that it would go bankrupt if no measures were taken to rectify the situation. They recently submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry in Beijing to have the commercial shares take over responsibility. The Ministry of Industry also believed that the government shares had not achieved any results after several years of management and that the mining business was deteriorating. Therefore, it approved the request and appointed Wu Shucai of the commercial shares as the general manager of the company and Zhou Ziheng as the assistant manager. Zhou first went to Lieshan to take over all affairs of the mine and then returned to Beijing to discuss improvement measures with Wu. It was recently heard that the board of directors of the mine held a meeting in Beijing on the 10th to retroactively approve Wu and Zhou as general manager and assistant manager to comply with the election procedures. This reorganization is purely the responsibility of the commercial shares, with no participation from the government shares. It is heard that the commercial shareholders have already raised funds. Once the internal affairs of the mine are rectified, they will purchase machinery, repair the coal and speed up mining, aiming to produce 500 tons of coal per day and promote sales as much as possible to develop the business. The general company here is in urgent need of the new general manager Wu Shucai to take over the affairs because there is no one in charge internally. The transfer procedure for the former general manager Huang has been completed and is ready for handover. (February 11)

Record of Songjiang First District Office Meeting 88

The First District Office held its thirty-ninth district affairs meeting on the 13th. More than ten township chiefs and assistants attended, with District Chief Zhong presiding. The meeting was conducted with formalities, and the work progress of the past month and routine cases were reported in detail. Matters discussed included: (1) The roster of the defense donation had been investigated for a long time, and there may have been changes in the middle. The county magistrate ordered a reinvestigation and report. The resolution was passed, and the township chiefs were responsible for the reinvestigation. (2) Regarding the repair of Tao Xing Bridge, the stonemasons had submitted accounts. How should it be carried out? Resolution: A bridge construction committee should be organized by local people to discuss funding and then rebuild. (3) The Finance Bureau was ordered by the province to merge. Should the collection of vehicle donations be taken back by this district for direct collection? Resolution passed. (4) The county is recruiting laborers to dredge the river, and a dredging committee has been established. How should this district handle it? Resolution: The First District River Dredging Committee should be organized, with the ten town chiefs (excluding the South Outer and North Outer Towns) as ex-officio members. In addition, enthusiastic people from this district will be hired as committee members, with a quota of forty-one people, to discuss funding and engineering matters. (5) The district regiment department proposed that a regular general training for members of the security corps be held as ordered. How should it be carried out? Resolution: Each township should send nine people, for a total of one hundred and eighty people in the district. Starting from March 1, they will be trained separately at designated locations in the four police districts. The district office will instruct the township police to be responsible for notifying the township regiment members. Other cases omitted.

Haimen County major bandits, Zhao Qingming, Cai Shunqi, etc., had committed numerous crimes. After being arrested, they were sentenced to death by the county court. Construction of Dajun Bridge River Intensifies 93

The dredging of the Dajun Bridge River and the repair of the abutments of the Dajun Bridge have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the southern abutment of the bridge was undermined when the mud downstream of the bridge was excavated, and the stone foundation loosened. The abutment suddenly sank by several inches, causing the Sun Siquan incense shop and Zaifeng Money Shop on the abutment to tilt, posing a danger. As a result, the shops temporarily suspended business to avoid danger. The Engineering Committee then discussed remedial measures, preparing to lay concrete under the bridge. The Lian Huai Delou's houses on the abutment have been demolished and work began today (13th) to lay concrete day and night. The revetments on both sides of the bridge are also being demolished and rebuilt. The engineering work is expected to be extended. Most of the revetment wharves of the rice shops on both sides of the river have been completed, and a few businesses are automatically pouring concrete and driving wooden stakes, which can also be completed within days.

Guerrilla Troops Arrive in Tongzhou to Suppress Mutinying Soldiers 95

The guerrilla troops stationed on the sea off Lüsi mutinied and became bandits at sea. On the 12th, the Anhui Provincial authorities transferred the guerrilla troops stationed in Zhenjiang, who arrived in Tongzhou aboard the Wushan wheel steamer, to proceed to Lüsi to join forces with the provincial and county police and militias to suppress the mutinying soldiers.

The Boundary of Mingguang County is Fixed and Shall Not be Altered 96

The Zhangbaling area, originally belonging to Chuzhou County, was assigned to the jurisdiction of the new Jiashan County. Previously, the merchants and residents of the area submitted a petition to the Fifth District Administrative Inspectorate, requesting that it remain under the jurisdiction of the old county. This was forwarded to the provincial government for consideration. It is now heard that the petition has been rejected and that the assignment of the fortress to Jiashan is a settled matter and shall not be altered.

Yangzhou Plans to Install Bandit-Proof Telephones 97

Liao Chuliang, Director of the First Public Security Bureau, noted that bandit alarms frequently occur in the area outside the Northwest Gate, including Phoenix Bridge, Lüyang Village, and Shuangqiao, but are beyond immediate reach. It is now planned to install temporary telephones for rapid response in the event of bandit alarms. However, the cost of felling poles and installation is substantial, and efforts are underway to raise the necessary funds.

The Decline of Commerce in Huzhou and the Increase in Unemployment 98

Three years ago, this city was most prosperous in the money, cloth, silk, and crepe trades. There were as many as twenty-five money shops. Due to successive years of disaster and the impact of war, financial conditions have become extremely sluggish, leading to the successive closure of various shops. Last year, Desheng, Longchang, Zhenghe, and three other shops also declared liquidation. This year, Anyu and Deyu have ceased operations. Only Deyuan, Defu, Shenyi, Qingyu, and Jiufu, five shops, are able to continue operating. Although the remaining shops have the intention to close, it may not materialize. The silk and cloth industry has also suffered greatly in recent years. Only Dafeng had a surplus of over four thousand yuan last year after deducting official interest. The remaining shops are all losing money and are implementing strict austerity measures. Silk weaving factories showed slight improvement last year, but due to weak sales, factories have excessive inventories, preventing economic circulation. After stopping work at the end of the year, it was originally planned to resume work in mid-month. However, due to the current situation, the resumption of work has been postponed indefinitely. Therefore, there are approximately more than one thousand unemployed people in various industries.

The Shanghai-Suzhou Double Track Railway Bureau Begins Planning 105

How to Raise Funds Has Not Yet Been Determined

There are Many Difficulties in Reforming the Songhu Railway

The Ministry of Railways plans to add a double track between Suzhou and Shanghai. Minister Gu Mengyu once contacted the banking community during his previous visit to Shanghai. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency inquired about the progress of the plan from the Shanghai-Suzhou Railway Administration yesterday. The director of the General Affairs Department of the Administration, Mo Hengjian, told us the following:

Preparing a Double-Track Plan 106

According to him, this project plan cannot be implemented without careful consideration and concrete plans due to funding and other related matters. Therefore, although the Railway Administration has already started planning, it still needs expert research. In terms of funding, the cost of the rails alone is estimated to be about 4 million yuan. Due to the addition of double tracks, the increase in vehicles, the expansion of the factory, the addition of small stations, and the increase of existing stations, as well as the storage and switching of vehicles, etc., all must be carried out simultaneously in order to be effective. However, due to the close commercial relationship between Suzhou and Shanghai, it is imperative to add double tracks in order to remedy the current congestion and to plan for future prosperity. At the same time, there is also a similar plan for the Nanjing to Zhenjiang section, but the completion of the plan may still have to wait. As for future funding, whether it will be obtained through overdrafts from banks or direct loans from the banking community, the method has not yet been determined. The rumor that loans will be taken from the banking community is not only too early but also untrue.

Difficulties in Reforming the Songhu Railway 108

Afterwards, the reporter asked about the reform of the Songhu Railway. According to Mr. Mo, the reform of the Songhu Railway was originally suggested by Director Huang when he was in the Public Works Bureau. Currently, the railway has 14 trains per day, which is ten fewer than before the war. The reason is partly that the vitality of Wusong has not recovered after the war, and partly that all the steam cars were damaged during the war and have not yet been restored. However, after the city center area is realized in the future, the transportation of the Songhu Railway will still be an important position. Reform is also a necessity in fact. However, how to reform and how to proceed is worth studying. It can be reformed on the original basis, or it can be independent. As for vehicles, if diesel cars are used, they can indeed reduce gas and wind and waves. However, diesel engines and diesel oil must still be purchased from abroad, which inevitably adds another opportunity for foreigners to make a profit. Whether this benefit to foreigners is beneficial to the country should also be carefully considered. Coal is still available in our country. If diesel is used, it is completely necessary to purchase foreign goods. Therefore, there are still many difficulties in this plan, it is said.

Problems with Zhenru Station, etc. 109

When there are vehicles that can be transferred, it can be started. Direct exchanges between Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo are currently inconvenient for both freight and passengers due to the obstruction of the Qiantang River to the Cao'e River. Therefore, the Qiantang River Bridge has been planned to be implemented as soon as possible to facilitate transportation and smooth freight. As for the current sale of the North Station, it is rumored that someone is competing to sell it. However, it is not the time to do so before the temporary station on Song Park Road is completed. The land area of the North Station was destroyed during the war due to the original Mu list. In the future, the Land Bureau will need to remeasure it. It should be around 700 Mu, and the price per Mu is about 30,000 taels. However, this has not yet been determined.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Warns the Fish Industry Not to Undertake Sales of Counterfeit Inferior Fish 113

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the ice-fresh fish industry, the salted fish industry, and the cured meat industry associations yesterday, asking them not to undertake sales of counterfeit inferior fish. The letter stated: Sirs, on the 11th of this month, we received a letter from overseas Chinese in Canada signed by one of the Chinese nationals, stating that there is now a large batch of Japanese salted fish, commonly known as Qingchuan fish in Shanghai, totaling more than one thousand boxes, which have been repackaged as British goods to come to China. The boxes are printed with British salted fish and B.A.C. and other words. Although the fish are Canadian seafood, the fishermen are also Japanese thieves, and the sellers are all Japanese slaves. It is the same as renaming the Japanese fish Russian salmon. The offending fish have been loaded on the Canadian vessel Victoria ABYOFVictoria to Shen, and will arrive in Shanghai around February 20. However, we have witnessed the Japanese slaves personally caring for the ship and stamping the boxes. The Japanese slaves are subject to our country's strong restrictions, so they have to think of other ways to repackage and change their names to deceive us Chinese people. We have witnessed it and must inform our compatriots, lest you patriotic gentlemen be deceived by them. Therefore, we first drafted this letter to respectfully inform you, and then ask you to warn the Shanghai Fish Trade Association and the local people of Shanghai. Please everyone save some last blood and show some conscience. Do not seek small profits and be greedy for cheap things, and forget national hatred. Unanimously refuse to buy, etc. After investigating and stating each section, it does not seem to be fabricated out of thin air. Since the ship will arrive in Shanghai around the 20th of this month, the more than 2,000 boxes of counterfeit inferior fish will naturally have to be sold by the fish traders in this city on their behalf. In addition to sending separate letters, the facts are notified to you to check and strictly warn your colleagues. When the inferior fish arrive, do not say that you are buying them. This is the most important thing.

The Municipal Government Prepares to Levy Land Value Tax 117

According to the Central News Agency, the land tax that this city originally intended to levy has been ordered by the central government to be changed to a land value tax. Yesterday, according to a spokesperson for the municipal government, the municipal government has now received an order from the central government stating, in brief, that the land value tax in this city can be levied immediately. The method of levying should be submitted to the Ministries of Finance and Interior for review and discussion before a reply is issued and the order is executed. The municipal government believes that the tax is a new creation, and the preparation procedures are particularly complex. Therefore, it has instructed the Bureaus of Finance and Land to plan immediately. The levying will commence as soon as the order is received.

The Dispute Between the Sugar Industry and Other Merchants, Direct Negotiation Was Ineffective 118

The Focus Remains on the Conversion Standard

The Sugar Industry Believes That Others Are Presumptuous

Other Merchants Have Submitted a Request to the Government to Prohibit

There Is No Choice But to Seek Other Solutions

The Sugar, Northern Goods, and Other Merchants United Market and the Sugar, Northern Goods, and Other Merchants are in disagreement with other merchants regarding the conversion of the new standard scale. Direct negotiation failed the night before. Other merchants have reported to the competent authorities requesting prohibition. Details are recorded below.

Negotiation Fails: Other Merchants Association and Sugar Industry Association negotiated on the method the night before. Representatives Zheng Zenan, Jiang Zhenbang and others from the sugar industry insisted on the 85% discount based on the government order to implement the new standard scale and the joint market resolution regarding the conversion method. Representatives Gong Jingyan, Ni Fu, etc. of the other merchants believed that the new standard scale should have an 84% discount when converted with the traditional scale. After a long period of debate, no results were achieved and the meeting dispersed.

Opinions of Both Sides: A reporter from the New Voice Newspaper visited committee members from both the sugar industry and other merchants. 1) Representatives from other merchants, Ni Fu, etc., stated that the traditional scales were 14 taels and 4 qian, while the new standard scales were 13 taels and 6 qian and 4 fen, a difference of 95%. The sugar industry's 85% conversion rate should be changed to 84%, and the northern goods' 88% conversion rate should be changed to 87%. Other industries such as washing medicine have already implemented these changes, otherwise they should be handled according to the old rules. Furthermore, this case should not be handled by the united market because members of the united market are mostly from the sugar industry and the northern goods industry. 2) Sugar industry representatives such as Zheng Zenan stated that the actions of other merchants are using the excuse of arguing over industry regulations and forcing the sugar industry to stop trading, which is regrettable. The change to the standard scale is based on the instructions of the Social Bureau. The 85% discount is actually in accordance with the resolution of the united market. Therefore, the sugar industry has implemented the change to the new system starting January 26th. The united market notified the other merchants of this resolution as early as October 30th of last year. The other merchants did not raise any objections within the acceptance period. Now, at the time of implementation, they suddenly raise objections, which is just causing trouble for themselves and others. The sale of sugar to this street only accounts for less than 10% of the total. Since the Shanghai war was resolved, the sugar in various other stores has been purchased from their own merchants. Therefore, their purchase from the sugar industry is even smaller. Therefore, if other merchants want to stop trading, they are presumptuous and can still operate as usual. The sugar industry believes that since the new system has been promoted, it is difficult to change it again. Otherwise, with the large number of sugar customers in Shanghai, it will cause a domino effect. Therefore, no matter what, the sugar industry cannot change the current new system. Regarding the shortening of the bank draft period and the pound sterling period, due to the high price of gold in recent years and the sudden increase in taxes, the price of sugar has doubled compared to the past. If the bank draft period is too long, the risk is too great and it is difficult to turnover funds. Therefore, it is necessary to shorten it to provide support. As for the use of bank drafts, it was originally a fixed rule. The acceptance of checks in recent years has been lenient and accommodating. Now, in view of the fact that the checks paid by other merchants for sugar in recent years have often been untrustworthy, and the sugar industry has suffered a lot, it has no choice but to decide to accept bank drafts in order to ensure the safety of the funds. If the association can guarantee the trustworthiness of the checks of its members, the sugar industry may still be willing to negotiate.

Request for Prohibition: The Other Merchants Association submitted to the Social Bureau and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating that they are requesting to be prohibited from changing the discount rate. They have been buying goods from merchants using traditional scales, and the standards and discounts for goods have been set. On January 26th of this year, they received a notice from the Sugar, Sea, North-South Miscellaneous Goods United Market that all industries should change to standard scales from that day onwards. It is the law that all industries should obey the standard scales. The sugar industry and the northern goods industry claim to be changing to standard scales, but in reality, they are still operating under the old rules, maintaining the 96% discount. After repeated consultations, they have not been approved. The northern goods industry secretly ordered runners not to put goods on the market, monopolizing the market. They should be held responsible for this. Under these adverse circumstances, the merchants in various shops have no goods to buy and have no choice but to seek other solutions in order to awaken the other party. Therefore, they are submitting this document to request the authorities to quickly prohibit the two industries and order them to set another scale discount, which should be handled in accordance with the established rules of each industry in order to maintain commercial difficulties.

Various Trade Associations Advocate for Chinese Merchant Insurance 119

The various trade associations of this city held an important meeting yesterday at the Commercial Association. Representatives from more than 60 trade associations, including the Sugar Industry, Mercerized Cotton Weaving Industry, Fireworks Industry, Color Printing Industry, Local Goods Industry, Ginseng Industry, Silk Industry, Sausage Industry, Paper Industry, Mineral Ash Industry, Cotton Cloth Industry, Coal Industry, Bean and Rice Industry, Rice Shop Industry, Woolen Fabric Industry, etc., including Lu Wenshao, Luo Qinghua, Ye Jiaxing, Chen Songyuan, Zheng Chengqing, Ma Shaoquan, Zhu Binglu, Lu Fengzhu, Mao Chunpu, Qiu Liangyu, Xie Zhongle, Gu Jiuru, Jin Runxiang, Ge Jechen, and others, totaling over a hundred people, elected Luo Qinghua as chairman. The chairman first reported on the importance of the insurance business and that various industries, in view of this, have organized the General Insurance Managers Co., Ltd. The company's business policy is to fully promote Chinese merchant insurance and protect the interests of policyholders, hoping that various industries will promote it extensively in order to regain rights. The following important cases were then discussed and resolved: 1) In the future, all types of insurance in various industries should, as far as possible, be entrusted to the General Insurance Managers Office of various industries in Shanghai for handling. 2) Various types of insurance in various industries that were previously managed by foreign merchants should be gradually transferred to Chinese merchants in the future. 3) All industries should be notified to organize insurance branch management offices, named as (General Insurance Managers Office of Various Industries in Shanghai, Branch Management Office of a Certain Industry), etc.

Negotiations Will Commence Between the Two Parties After the Collision Between the Ningbo and Taiping Ships 120

There are Continued Requests for Compensation from Ships Involved

After the collision between the Taiping ship of the Taigu Company and the Ningbo ship of the Zhongwei Company, the two parties will conduct negotiations. The families of the victims have requested compensation, and there are continued requests for compensation from civilian ships damaged in the collision. Details are recorded below.

Negotiations Between the Two Parties: After the two companies, Taigu and Zhongwei, sent surveyors to jointly investigate the ship damage the day before, the damage to the Taigu ship was heavier than that to the Ningbo ship. Yesterday, the repairs to the Taiping ship were put out to tender, and the British-owned Yesong Shipyard won the bid to repair it. The price is 1,450 taels, and the deadline is five days, starting today. It is heard that the Zhongwei Company has hired a notary public and will submit reasons to negotiate with the Taigu Company within days. It is also heard that the Taigu Company will also hire a notary public to determine the responsibility for the collision.

Request for Compensation: There were also Chen Qilang's civilian ship, Kong Fuyuan's sand ship, and Ye Ruicheng's sand ship, etc., which were affected, requesting the two companies to compensate for the losses. In addition, there was the boatman Hu Yuxiang, 23 years old, from Yancheng, who made a living by rowing boats. The sampan he was rowing that day was No. 1190. The boat cracked and sank, and he fell into the water on the spot. His body has not been found. Yesterday, his wife, Yang, sent a letter to the Zhongwei Company requesting compensation.

Representatives of Steamships Petitioned Yesterday 121

Regarding the Tragedy of the Wusong Steamer

The Wusong steamer of the British-owned Taigu Company had a tragedy. Despite repeated mediation by party and government agencies, it has not yet been resolved. Yesterday, 37 steamships, including Anqing, Gonghe, Ruihe, Suzhou, Changsha, Nanyang, Xinming, and Jihe, sent representatives Lu Shuangxi, Song Dingxun, Zhao Jianquan, Jiang Youqing, etc., with a petition to the municipal government, requesting that they forward it to the party and government agencies in Hankou to guarantee that they could resume work as soon as possible. Zhang Yinyu, a staff member of the First Section of the Municipal Government, received them. First, the petition representatives stated their intentions and submitted the petition. Mr. Zhang replied that the case had been transferred by the central government to the Hankou Municipal Party Committee and Municipal Government for handling and advised the representatives to wait quietly for a resolution. The petition is recorded below: We respectfully request that the Hankou Municipal Party and Government agencies guarantee the resumption of work for the workers. The Wusong steamship violated the previous reconciliation record No. 225, violently expelled workers, and caused a tragedy. The details of what happened have been reported to your government for strict negotiations. Subsequently, the British-owned Taigu Company instigated detectives to obstruct the resumption of work for the workers. We have submitted another document to request that you forward it to the Hankou Municipal Government to guarantee the resumption of work according to the agreement. However, the time has been delayed until now, and we have not been approved. For this reason, we are jointly submitting a follow-up petition, requesting your review and approval, and that you immediately forward the reconciliation record and relevant documents related to this case to the Hankou Municipal Government to handle it according to the agreement and guarantee the resumption of work. This will be a great benefit. We respectfully submit this to the Municipal Government.

It Is Difficult to Increase Postage for Southeast Asia 122

Regarding the issue of increasing postage for the Southeast Asian Islands and the Federated Malay States, the amount proposed by the General Post Office of this city is to increase the rate for each letter weighing over 20 grams from 5 cents to 12.5 cents. After submitting it to the Ministry of Communications, due to the impact on the burdens of overseas Chinese, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission was immediately consulted. Yesterday, according to a person in charge of the post office, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, after receiving the letter from the Ministry of Communications, convened a standing committee on the 11th to discuss it. The result was that increasing postage to the Southeast Asian Islands and the Federated Malay States would have a significant impact on the livelihoods of overseas Chinese. Moreover, in this era of commercial depression, the daily hard work of overseas Chinese is still insufficient to pay local taxes and miscellaneous expenses. How can they bear the burden of increased postage from their home country? Therefore, they have replied to the Ministry of Communications, firmly opposing it. It is expected that this issue will be difficult to implement.

The Case of Li Yushan of Shashi Textile Company is Awaiting Further Hearing 125

If Li Fails to Appear, an Arrest Warrant Will Be Issued

The Shashi Textile Company was established in Shashi, Hubei Province, three years ago and is operating quite well, with profits of hundreds of thousands of yuan. For the convenience of its shareholders, the company has established a Shanghai office at 3 Sanhe Lane, Jiangxi Road, with General Manager Li Yushan holding exclusive power. For the past three years, shareholder and board meetings have never been convened as required to report on business conditions, issue dividends, or distribute bonuses. One of the shareholders, Yin Geru, holds shares worth 10,000 yuan. Since he has neither received dividends nor interest, he sold his shares last December and demanded over 5,000 yuan in dividends and interest from Li. Li refused to pay a single penny and, together with the accountant Yu Yingle, insulted Yin. Yin sued them, and the First Special District Court found the accusations to be true, giving Li and Yu a light punishment as a warning. In addition to this case, Yin also filed a criminal lawsuit against Li personally, accusing him of embezzlement, fraud, and falsifying accounts. A preliminary hearing has already been held, as reported previously. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi of the First Special Court held another hearing. The defendant Li Yushan did not appear, only his defense lawyer. The lawyer stated that the case is currently being mediated by Du Shaoru, the chairman of the Shashi Company, and requested a postponement. However, the plaintiff Yin Geru denied the mediation. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the defendant Li Yushan is actually evading justice. Although the defendant has published a rebuttal in the newspaper regarding the four charges made by the plaintiff, it only makes his desire to cover up his actions more obvious. The witness summoned, Gao Jiaren, the executive director of the company, has already appeared and should be questioned. Witness Gao testified that the Shashi Company was established three years ago and is operating profitably. No board meetings were initially held. A meeting was held yesterday, but he did not attend due to a throat ailment. However, he heard that the accounts have not yet been cleared and that dividends have never been issued. He was aware that Yin Geru subscribed to shares, but he did not know that Yin sold his shares until Yin demanded dividends from Li Yushan, and a dispute ensued. Judge Wu then ordered that the hearing be postponed to the afternoon of the 17th of this month and that the defendant Li Yushan be summoned to appear for further questioning. If he continues to evade justice, an arrest warrant will be issued.

Fire in Nanshi 126

Kong Abao, a 34-year-old man from Suzhou, a resident of 318 Dalin Road in Nanshi, was careless while cooking breakfast on the mezzanine at around 10 AM yesterday. In an instant, the fire intensified, piercing the roof and spreading to the corner buildings at 1, 2, and 3 Fangxiehou Road, the Shaxunxing Bamboo Shop opened by Chen Wangshi of Zhoujiaham, Pudong Dragon King Temple. Fortunately, the police officers from the Tangjajie Police Station of the Second District General Administration of the Municipal Public Security Bureau heard the news and immediately reported to the fire brigades, which rushed to the scene to put out the fire with all their strength. The fire was extinguished in about half an hour. It is estimated that four flat houses were burned. At the time, nearby residents were moving and grabbing boxes and luggage, causing great chaos. The Second District Patrol Officer and other police officers arrived at the scene to suppress the situation, but the arsonist had already escaped without a trace. Only Chen Wangshi and Tang Jinsheng were arrested and taken to the police station for questioning.

Kangti Road Postal Branch Accepts Packages 127

According to postal news in this city, the Kangti Road branch will also handle the acceptance and posting of packages from today onwards to facilitate the public. The Township Head of Yinghu Township in Minhang District is Accused

County Magistrate Yan Instructs the District Head to Investigate

Hua Bishu, the township head of Yinghu Township in Minhang District, has been accused by citizens such as Jiang Dangsheng of the township of engaging in malpractices in the purchase and sale of land, failing to establish official contracts, arbitrarily writing consolidation certificates, and underreporting land prices to embezzle deed taxes. This was reported to the Shanghai County Government, and County Magistrate Yan ordered the district head to strictly investigate. After many days, Hua Bishu learned of this and wrote a letter claiming to represent the district head's intentions, forcing the landholders on both sides of the transaction to sign, intending to shift the blame. The landholders refused to sign and jointly submitted a petition to the Shanghai County Government, stating the facts. After receiving the petition, County Magistrate Yan again instructed the district head to investigate and report fairly.

Changes in County Public Security Bureau Chiefs 128

Since the Shanghai County Government moved to Beiqiao, it has strengthened the public security of the county and made large-scale changes to the chiefs of all public security branch bureaus. Specifically, Mao Yijun, chief of the Minhang First Branch Bureau, has been transferred to the Beiqiao Third Branch Bureau, and the vacancy has been filled by Zhao Lian, chief of the Louhang Second Branch Bureau. The vacancy left by Zhao, chief of the Second Branch Bureau, has been filled by Zhang Xingbang, chief of the Third Branch Bureau. In addition, Zhang Zhenyuan, chief of the Sanlin Fourth Branch Bureau, has been transferred to the county government and is awaiting appointment, and the vacancy has been filled by Mao Fang, chief of the Maqiao Sixth Branch Bureau. The vacancy left by the Sixth Branch Bureau has been temporarily filled by Zhao Wanli, a member of the bureau. Yesterday, County Magistrate Yan issued instructions to appoint them, ordering them to take over their respective positions.

Minutes of the Accountants Association Meeting 129

The Shanghai Accountants Association convened its eighth joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees yesterday. Members present included Li Wenjie, Bei Zuyi, Wang Haifan, Ye Danian, He Yuanming, Wang Yusheng, Jiang Wanping, Yang Daxun, and Xie Lin. 1) The meeting opened as usual. 2) Member Wang Haifan chaired the meeting. 3) Member Wang Haifan reported that the association had completed the investigation of losses from the Shanghai War, which was jointly handled by the association, the Social Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The expenses amounted to 2,162.87 yuan, which was divided equally among the three organizations. The association's share was 920.956 yuan, with a copy of the income and expenditure statement, a distribution list of the surplus funds, and a copy of all accounting records. Should this amount be paid from the association's surplus fund from previous years? It was decided that it should be temporarily listed as a borrowed fund, pending a decision at the spring members' meeting. 4) The standing committee reported on a letter from the preparatory committee for the memorial service for Camp Commander An, who died in the defense of Yuguan Pass, requesting that the association send elegiac couplets, flower gardens, etc., and send representatives to participate in the mourning. In addition to the association sending elegiac couplets, should representatives be sent to participate? It was decided to send Committee Member Xie Lin and Committee Member Yang Daxun as representatives. 5) The Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau's instruction No. 7901 stated that it had previously submitted a request for an interpretation of Article 16 of the Certified Public Accountant Regulations and was instructed to request the Executive Yuan to forward it to the Judicial Yuan for interpretation before complying. 6) The Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau's instruction No. 8186 stated that the request to amend the articles of association had not been approved by the Ministry. 7) The Shanghai Municipal Government sent a letter stating that it had resolved the method of clearing goods seized by the Anti-Japanese Association and was scheduled to hold a meeting, requesting that the association appoint representatives to attend to discuss the proceedings. It was decided to notify Committee Member Jiang Wanping and Committee Member Yu Xiji to attend as representatives. 8) The Shanghai Lawyers Association sent a letter stating that it would like to appoint a member to review the income and expenditure report for the second half of the 21st year in order to ensure fairness. It was decided to appoint Committee Member Xie Lin and Member Qin Kai to conduct the review and to directly entrust members of the association to handle this matter in the future. 9) Committee Member Bei Zuyi and Committee Member Li Wenjie proposed that the association should stipulate a unified standard for the procedures for members to perform their professional duties. It was decided to pass the proposal and appoint Bei Zuyi, Li Wenjie, Xie Lin, Jiang Wanping, Pan Xulun, Xu Yongzuo, Xi Taishu, Wang Haifan, Chen Riping, and other nine people as members, to be convened by Committee Member Bei Zuyi. 10) Member Lin Benzhong sent a letter asking whether the word "review" in Article 6 of the general outline of business tax collection in various provinces implies auditing or inspection, or only numerical calculations, and what the procedures are. It was decided to appoint Committee Member Li Wenjie to review. 11) Member Zhang Yonghui sent a letter stating that he had no time to perform his duties and would like to temporarily withdraw from the association. It was decided that he would be allowed to withdraw from the association after paying his outstanding fees. 12) Accountants Zhu Xinmin and Chen Guoquan requested to join the association. It was decided to approve their request.

Achievements of Chinese Photography Exhibits at the Chicago Expo 133

Only About 500 Selected from 2,000 Submitted Photos and Negatives

Photos of Chinese Border Regions and the Dunhuang and Yungang Grottoes are Most Valuable

丨Setting a New Record for Chinese Photography Exhibitions丨

The China Travel Service was commissioned by the Chicago Exposition Preparatory Committee to collect Chinese photography exhibits for display in the United States. Mr. Chen Xiangtao, the director of the service, considered this matter to be of great importance to international prestige. He specifically assigned responsible personnel to collect the exhibits and invited contemporary celebrities to form a committee to guide and judge the works. After three months of preparation, the project is nearing completion. The details are as follows:

Preparatory Process: At the beginning of the preparations, Mr. Chen Xiangtao, the director of the service, invited contemporary celebrities Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Chu Minyi, Xia Jingguan, Zheng Wuchang, Lang Jingshan, Chen Wanli, Guo Shuliang, Jiang Xiaojian, Shao Xunmei, Wang Xiaoting, and Mrs. Schubert to be members of the committee. Fortunately, they all generously accepted. After several meetings, the photography collection event was divided into seven groups to handle: (1) Famous scenic spots and landscapes in various places, (2) Historical sites and cultural relics with historical or artistic value, (3) Famous buildings, both ancient and modern, (4) Various modern new constructions, (5) Items and customs that can be used for academic reference, (6) Fine art photography works, (7) In addition to the above regulations, excellent works may be selectively adopted. Once the outline was determined, solicitations were sent to various institutions, groups, and individuals. A reception was once held for photographers in the local area, and several meetings were held, all chaired by Mr. Ye Gongchuo. Mr. Ye considered this matter to be related to international honor and solicited from all parties in his personal capacity, so the results exceeded expectations. This is especially appreciated by the service.

List of Exhibitors: The institutions that participated in this solicitation included the Guangzhou, Hankou, and Qingdao Municipal Governments, the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, the Qingdao Agricultural and Forestry Office, the Port Authority, the Observatory, the Ministry of Railways, the Ministry of Communications, the International Telegraph Administration, the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau, the Bureau of Entomology, the National Economic Council, the National Road Construction Association, and others. Groups included the Guangzhou Far East Pictures and News Agency, the Jiaxing Photography Society, the Songjiang Huating Photography Society, various universities, and major photography studios in various ports. Individuals included Chu Minyi, Li Wenji, and Huang Ying in [Nanjing]; Li Yaosheng, Zhao Cheng, and Sun Weikuan in [Beiping]; Chen Jiazhen and Li Lansun in [Jinan]; Su Zhuying, Liu Yunxiu, Yuan Shuhuang, and Hu Zhujiang in [Qingdao]; Zhang Jingbo and Lu Yucang in [Henan]; Xiang Huian in [Zhenjiang]; Wu Zhongxing and Zhuang Zenghu in [Changzhou]; Chen Wanli, Zhong Zhenxin, and Zhai Peiqing in [Hangzhou]; Yang Peng and Yan Yushi in [Hunan]; Xia Shaoqiu in [Wenzhou]. In this area, there were Fu Bingchang, Gan Naiguang, Lang Jingshan, Lin Jin, Zhou Jianqiao, Feng Sizhi, Ruan Siqi, Wang Yuhuai, Tong Bo, Chen Rentao, Zhang Mingguang, Cao Zuguang, Su Jinyuan, Huang Lianzhang, Chen Zhili, Chen Yuansu, Shen Yan, Wang Dafo, Hu Xianyun, Gu Bowei, Shu Xincheng, Shao Yuxiang, Zhang Pansun, Mo Tianxiang, Zhang Daqian, Zuo Gengsheng, Huang Zhongchang, Liu Xucang, Xu Zuyin, Chen De, and over a hundred others. A total of over a thousand photos and over eight hundred negatives were received. The work of enlarging the negatives was handled by Mr. Lang Jingshan, and the rest was handled by Mr. Zhang Ruiliu, a famous photographer at Watson's, so each photo is very exquisite and impressive.

Brief Summary of Contents: The content of the photography exhibits is mostly fine art, followed by famous scenic spots and historical sites. Among them, the most valuable are the photos of Manchuria, Qinghai, Tibet, Mongolia, Gansu, Xinjiang, and other border regions, which are mostly unseen by outsiders and are very difficult to obtain. There are also many photos related to academic aspects, such as Yungang stone Buddhas and Dunhuang murals. After repeated evaluations and summaries by the committee, only over five hundred points were selected for inclusion.

Mounting Work: The service also paid special attention to the mounting work. The cardboard used is Chinese gold, which is very elegant. An English description is embedded in the frame. Mr. Lang Jingshan is currently working with the service staff day and night to complete the frames. It will be completed within a day or two.

Scheduled Exhibition: The Chicago Expo Preparatory Committee is scheduled to open the exhibition at the Academia Sinica on the 18th of this month. These photography exhibits will also be sent for display at the same time. However, due to the small space, they cannot be fully exhibited. The service plans to hold a large-scale photography exhibition at a suitable location after the end of the exhibition, displaying all the exhibits for the public to appreciate. Once the date is determined, it will be announced in the newspaper.

Verdict in the Chen Tugeng Case 134

Chen Claims He Was Mistakenly Released by the Prison Guard

Official Questions Why He Confessed in the Second District

Ling Jiannan, a native of Chuansha living at 20 Ningkang Lane, West Gate, was killed by a mob hired by dismissed detective Wang Wencai and others. Chen Tugeng was apprehended at the scene. Later, he was mistakenly released from the prison and was re-apprehended. The prosecutor indicted Chen Tugeng, Huang Shaoying, and Huang Zicheng, who was accused of harboring Wang Wencai. The hearing continued yesterday with Judge Qian presiding. Chen Tugeng stubbornly denied committing the murder. Regarding his escape from the prison, he claimed that it was the prison guard's mistake and had nothing to do with him. The judge questioned why he confessed to using an axe to attack someone in the Second District, to which he claimed he had never said that and that he had been beaten. Huang Shaoying testified that he did not go to the murder scene and that he was crippled and could not commit the crime. Huang Zicheng testified that Wang Wencai was not his apprentice, that he did not know him, and that he did not harbor him. However, the deceased's mother, Ling Wangshi, brought her grandson to the court and still accused the defendants of being suspects and murderers. At this point, Prosecutor Wu appeared in court to state his opinion, saying that Chen Tugeng was apprehended at the scene, and Huang Shaoying and Huang Zicheng were accused by the plaintiff, and requested that they be sentenced according to the law. After the lawyers' defenses, the judge declared the debate closed and the verdict will be announced on the 22nd.

Autopsy of Russian Bodyguard Killed in Zheng Xitang Kidnapping 135

Zheng's Own Injuries Progressing Well

Zheng Xitang, manager of the Ping'an Shipping Company, accompanied by deputy manager Chen Yisheng and Russian bodyguard Fan Xilisaisufu, left the company's South City branch at approximately 2:00 PM on the 11th of this month after finishing their business. As they were about to board their car, several kidnappers who had been lying in wait rushed out. One kidnapper pointed a gun at Chen Yisheng and ordered him to return to the company. Chen then heard gunshots, and both Zheng and the Russian bodyguard had been shot and wounded by the kidnappers. The kidnappers failed to kidnap Zheng and fled. Zheng was taken to a hospital in the South City for treatment, and the Russian was taken to the Tongren Hospital. However, the Russian succumbed to his injuries and died. The hospital reported to the Hongkou Police Department, who sent detectives to investigate. The body was then taken to the Rou Lun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court commissioned Prosecutor Guo Wei to go to the morgue to examine the body. Chen Yisheng, 41 years old, testified that as they were about to get into the car, the kidnappers rushed out and forced him back into the company. He only ran to the stairs when he heard gunshots and did not see the kidnappers' faces clearly. The driver, Zhang Xilin, also testified. Prosecutor Guo then determined that the deceased Russian, Fan Xilisaisufu, died of gunshot wounds inflicted by the kidnappers. The body was handed over to Jigu Guguinuo (transliteration) who signed for it and took it away for burial. It was also learned that Zheng Xitang himself was still at the Tongren Hospital, where he was undergoing surgery by Dr. Gao, the head of surgery. He was conscious. Yesterday morning, his son, Zheng Hao, told people that his father's injuries were progressing well and his fever had not increased. He was already drinking porridge. However, according to the doctor's orders, he could not use his brain, so he had not received any visitors in recent days.

Changbang Rice Merchants Oppose the New Six-Dou Rice Measure 138

Changbang Rice Merchants Oppose Shanghai Merchants' New Six-Dou Measure, telegram reads: We believe that national legislation must conform to public opinion and long-standing customs, and that legislation and custom must exist in parallel. It has never been the case that the convenience of a few should disrupt the established system and force the majority to obey. Recently, the government has been promoting the new system of weights and measures, and merchants and people are also abandoning the old and welcoming the new in order to comply. However, Shanghai merchants have suddenly had a strange idea, taking advantage of the transition between the old and new measurement instruments, taking the opportunity to profit privately by creating a six-dou capacity measure to exploit merchants. This is neither in line with the old system nor does it violate the new measure. They use the convenience of packing and customs declaration as an excuse to deceive the government and oppress the merchants, disregarding national laws and abandoning market credit. Their means are pervasive, and their malpractice is growing. The sales of rice in Shanghai are most prosperous from Changshu, and it is most affected by this erosion. Therefore, our Changbang rice merchants vow not to recognize this private six-dou measure and will investigate the inside story. Packing and customs declaration are export operations. Those who eat rice and specialize in export operations are even more deplorable. We hereby report the facts and request that your government ministries and bureaus comply with public opinion, conduct a fair investigation and prohibit it, so as to comply with the laws and regulations for promoting measurement and enriching the people's food supply in the future. The gratitude of the merchants will be overwhelming. In addition to separate telegrams to the Ministry of Industry, the Municipal Government, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, we respectfully telegram Shanghai Changbang Rice Merchants Jin Weixiang et al., 250 people.

Fire on Broadway Kills People 139

Five Houses and Two Floors Burned Down

Charred Body Suspected to Be a Missing Apprentice

Zou Xingji Carpentry Shop at 933 Broadway, with the workers' dormitory upstairs, had several apprentices gathered upstairs during their spare time playing card games until about 1:00 AM last night when they turned off the lights and went to sleep. Unexpectedly, around 2:00 AM, a pile of wood shavings in the room suddenly caught fire, likely caused by the apprentices carelessly discarding cigarette butts. At that time, the workers were still sound asleep and did not notice. When the fire spread and extended to the floorboards, they were awakened from their dreams. Seeing the room full of fire, with no way out, they quickly pushed open the windows facing the street and jumped down to escape, without raising an alarm. As a result, the fire spread, and when it reached the Mei Li Leather Shop at 932 next door, the owner, Xu Yongqi, noticed and quickly shouted for help. At the same time, the neighbors were awakened. However, due to the dry weather and the wind, the fire soon spread to the Fa Li Western Clothing Store at 931 and the Yuan Shuntai Steel Trunk Shop at 934 on the left. The Yi Shun Tarpaulin Shop at 935 was also affected. Seeing the fire spreading, the firefighters divided the hoses to extinguish the fire from behind, fearing that it would spread to the adjoining houses on Huaji Road. After an hour, the fire was slightly subdued, but the Maolong Tarpaulin Shop at 930 and the Fu Rongtai Antique Shop at 929 had two floors affected and burned. The windows and doors on the upper floors of 941 and 942 Yuanfang Lane on Huaji Road were also almost burned, but fortunately, the firefighters worked hard to extinguish the fire, which prevented it from being destroyed. It was not until 5:00 AM that the fire was extinguished. As a result, five houses from 931 to 935 and two floors of 929 and 930 were destroyed. Mei Li Leather Shop owner Xu Yongqi and his wife, Ms. Gu, were burned on their backs while moving items from the fire. Chen Chuanfang, 38, a cook at Zou Xingji Carpentry Shop, from Haimen, broke his right leg after jumping from the window after the fire started. They were all taken to the Tongren Hospital by the fire truck and are not in danger. After the investigation, an apprentice from Zou Xingji Carpentry Shop, named Long Gao, 17 years old, from Haimen, was missing. Later, firefighters found a charred corpse in the rubble. The limbs were broken. According to the neighbors, it was likely the apprentice, who was crushed by something while hiding and burned to death, which is also a tragedy.

Verdict in the Private Counterfeit Money Case 140

Detective Shen Dehui of the Huishi Police Department, along with detective Jin Haibo, arrested nine men and women, Zhou Baosheng, Cao Jinbao, Chen Yushan, Chen Wangshi, Zhang Rongqing, Lu Wenxiang, He Zhangshi, Cao Lianheng, and Cai Luozhang, who were privately hiding counterfeit money in Room 28 of the Anle Hotel on North Zhejiang Road and at 247 Lafayette Road in the French Concession on January 24th. They seized ten counterfeit ten-yuan bills and seventy-five counterfeit five-yuan bills. They also raided the private manufacturing facility at 57 Li's House in Beishiqiao, Dachang Town, and confiscated the printing equipment. They were brought back to the police station and sent to the First Special District Court. After repeated interrogations, the case has been concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Qian Wenji appeared in court and announced the verdict. Zhou Baosheng was sentenced to six years in prison. Chen Yushan and Chen Wangshi were each sentenced to four years in prison. Cao Jinbao, Zhang Rongqing, and He Zhangshi were each sentenced to two years and six months in prison. Lu Wenxiang, Cao Lianheng, and Cai Luozhang were acquitted. The confiscated counterfeit money and equipment were confiscated.

Each Barrel of Fish Charged Twenty Yuan

Full Payment Agreed Yesterday Morning

Ships such as the Jiangjing and others had a total of over two hundred barrels seized, causing negotiations among fish merchants in Shanghai. This matter was reported in this newspaper. It was only resolved yesterday. The details are recorded as follows:

Fish Merchants' Request: The fresh fish seized from ships such as the Jiangjing, Jiangxin, and Xinjiangtian by the South Wharf Manager Li on Saturday totaled more than 240 barrels. They have been deposited in the Jinliyuan Wharf warehouse for two days. The fresh goods are滞留ed and most likely to rot. Yesterday morning, representatives of various phototypesetting companies went to the Merchant Steamship Company to negotiate with Liu Hongsheng, requesting to pick up the goods first to avoid significant losses due to spoilage. The fish merchants are willing to double the freight and pay a fine of six yuan per barrel.

Ordered to Pay Guarantee Money: Liu Hongsheng met with the fish merchants and refused to accept the fine, saying that loading fresh goods on the ships was a business, but the procedures taken by the fish merchants were not in compliance.

Detailed Account of Xiao Xin'an's Suicide 143

Thinking of Becoming an Editor in Surabaya After School Salary Reduction

Severing Relations with Her Brother as a Distant Cause of Suicide

The suicide case of Ms. Xiao Xin'an from Yixing has been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency received a letter from a friend in Ambon, Seram, reporting the details of Ms. Xiao's suicide. The account is quite detailed, and the contents are hereby provided to the press for the concern of those who care about the lady. (Above omitted.) Since the news of Ms. Xiao's death spread to various places, it has caused a sensation in the overseas Chinese community. I have made special trips to various places to investigate and learned the following about Ms. Xiao's suicide: Ms. Xiao had been working at Peide School for two and a half years and had always been on good terms with everyone. This year, the board of directors of Peide School was reorganized, and due to financial difficulties, a meeting was held to discuss ways to maintain operations. As a result, it was resolved to reduce teachers' salaries. It was considered that male teachers had family burdens and could not be reduced much, while female teachers earned and used their own money, and expenses were not large, so the salary was set at 60 guilders. Ms. Xiao's salary was originally 125 guilders, and she felt that such a large reduction was excessive and that the school's treatment was unbalanced, so she decided to leave. Later, she discussed it with Mr. Zeng, the director of studies at the school, and Mr. Zeng agreed to introduce her to the Surabaya Java Daily Telegraph as an editor. Xiao initially agreed, but two hours later, she came back to tell Zeng, "[I don't need to go to Surabaya]." Her words seemed to suggest that she had other plans, but in fact, the thought of suicide had already been decided in her heart. So, she mailed her savings of more than two hundred guilders (some say it was more than a thousand guilders) back to China and telegraphed her brother and relatives, saying, "[Do not send letters after my death]." The telegraph cost more than forty guilders. On the evening of the 15th, the lady handed a letter to the school servant, earnestly instructing him to mail it in the morning, and gave the school servant a reward of five guilders. After returning to her room, she pulled down the mosquito net from her bed, placed all her clothes and books on the ground in a circle, poured kerosene on them, and set them on fire. She then placed herself in the middle of the fire, allowing it to burn her. After a while, the fire became more intense, and she screamed in pain. The school servant heard the sound and saw the flames in the room from outside. He rushed to open the door, but it was locked. So, he knocked on the door and shouted loudly. The lady personally opened the door and let him in. At that time, the lady was completely on fire and had turned into a firebrand. The school servant was terrified at the sight and quickly fetched water to extinguish the flames. The lady calmly ordered the school servant to fetch a rattan couch for her to lie down on. At the same time, two male teachers who shared a room with the lady learned of the incident and quickly asked a doctor to come to the school to treat the lady. After examining her, the doctor said that her flesh was already charred and could not be saved, so he instructed the two teachers to quickly report the incident to the police. The lady was then taken to the hospital by car, but it was already twelve o'clock. When the police arrived at the hospital to see the lady, she was still able to speak and admitted to the police that it was suicide and that it had nothing to do with anyone else. She died at four o'clock in the morning on the 16th. After the lady's death, her brother telegraphed her from Shanghai. The telegram was signed and collected by the Kapitan. The telegram read (You are already dead, how can you send a telegram?) The lady telegraphed, telling him of her death, and her brother doubted it and questioned it. It is said that when the lady came south, her brother tried hard to stop her, and after the incident was discovered on the ship, her brother felt even more regret and wrote to her to sever their relationship. It is said that this was one of the reasons for the lady's suicide.

The First Batch of Hunan Rice is Shipped to Shanghai 144

One Million Bags to be Loaded to Shanghai in Three Months

The Hunan Rice Production and Sales Committee, commissioned Wang Huixian, delegated by committee members Tan Changkai and others, to come to Shanghai to discuss shipping arrangements with Sanbei and China Merchants. The shipping fee is charged at 60% of the fixed price. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. Now, the packaging contract between the two companies has been sent by the Production and Sales Committee yesterday, requesting Yu Qiaqing and Liu Hongsheng to sign it and send it back to Changsha. All the Hunan rice to be transported can be loaded to Shanghai first with one million bags in three months. The first batch of 13,200 bags, transported by the Sanbei steamer, can arrive in Shanghai today.

Pay the Fee and Pick Up the Fish The fish merchants followed Mr. Liu's instructions and immediately prepared the fees yesterday morning, totaling about 5,000 yuan, and sent them to the bureau as a certificate for picking up the goods. After receiving the payment, the bureau ordered the head of the Li warehouse to release the fish barrels, so the fish detained in the warehouse before 12 o'clock were completely picked up. A dispute has come to an end. Future Measures Mr. Liu convened the heads of various ships, the director of business and the owners of Jianglun ships yesterday to discuss that from now on, the transportation of fresh fish from the Yangtze River should be declared as ordinary passenger and cargo, and the bureau should issue a bill of lading. The fish should be picked up with the bill of lading when it arrives in Shanghai, turning private into public and eliminating smuggling. However, in consideration of the short wages of the sailors, five cents of ocean per barrel of water feet will be taken out and distributed to the sailors. In the future, if any private transport is found, it will be confiscated and heavily fined. At the same time, it was agreed that there will be two shipments of fish seedlings to Shanghai every year, which can be accommodated exceptionally. Seafood from North China and vegetables from Ningbo are also prohibited from being loaded and smuggled, so as to ensure that every drop of water returns to the public.

Yan Jinbiao's Appeal to the Supreme Court is Still Sentenced to Death 145

At 6 pm on August 15, 1920, a revenge shooting case by Jiangbei bandits occurred in Room 2 on the ground floor of the Fa Shang Hotel at No. 113 West Xinqiao Street, French Concession. As a result, Jiang Yizhong, Xia Yongsheng, and Mr. Xue were killed, and Zhong Ziqing was injured. The murderer escaped. Later, Jin Jiulin, inspector of the special agency of the French Concession Police, and Qian Yumin, detective, arrested the murderer Yan Jinbiao, also known as Yan Dongbo, in Tiancheng Lane, Maixi Ni Road, the next day. It was also found that Yan had robbed Huang Dingchang's South Goods Store, Qiu Zhoumao, and Shen Huating's stores three times before the incident. He was sent to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. Yan confessed that he was instructed by Li Guocheng to commit the revenge killing and committed three robbery cases. After trial, Yan was found guilty of premeditated murder and sentenced to death. He was sentenced to imprisonment for each of the three robbery cases and executed. Yan refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, but the appeal was rejected. Yan still refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Supreme Court. Li Guocheng, who instigated the crime, was arrested by the Public Security Bureau in the Chinese Concession in the winter of that year for another case. He was brought back by the Second Special Court for trial. Due to the investigation of evidence, the trial has not been concluded. It is now known that Yan's third trial appeal has been concluded by the Supreme Court. Except for a slight change in the robbery charge, the murder charge is still executed according to the original sentence. The judgment has been sent to the Third Branch of the High Court and other courts, and the police were dispatched yesterday to deliver the judgment. The death penalty will be executed soon.

Local Court Burns Narcotics 146

The Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office burned 3,594 items of opium, narcotics, and smoking paraphernalia from October to December of last year at 9 am yesterday on the open space west of the court. It had previously submitted a request to the superior court and various agencies to send personnel to supervise. Representatives who arrived at the court yesterday included Zhu Jun of the High Court Prosecutor's Office, Zhao Shizhao of the Third Branch of the High Court, Ju Zhijing of the First Special Court, Zheng Youshang of the Command Headquarters, Huang Chen of the Municipal Government, Wu Fengwen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Wei Shilin of the County Government, Ren Bin of the Municipal Party Department, and Li Yunzeng of the Anti-Drug Association. They were greeted and hosted by Court President Shen Xiqing and Chief Prosecutor Lou Ying to the supervision site. Police Chief Chen Junfang and Police Officers Chen Xiwei and Zhu Wenqing were ordered to supervise the police to carry out the narcotics. After weighing and counting them on the spot, they were set on fire with pine firewood, kerosene, and salt. The fire was completed in the afternoon, and the ashes were packed in hemp bags and sunk in the Huangpu River to eliminate the poisonous atmosphere.

The Greyhound Association's Lawsuit Continues to be Heard 147

The Greyhound Association's lawsuit against Martin, the extra general patrol of the Public Works Department, and Maikenaiden, the former chairman, continued to be heard yesterday morning at the British Court. The plaintiff's lawyer, Harris, responded to the reasons given by the defendant's lawyer for requesting the dismissal of the case, especially focusing on the defendant's lawyer's claim that the two defendants were only performing official duties and acting on the orders of the Public Works Department, and that the plaintiff must prove that the Public Works Department had violated civil law. He argued that the case was against the two defendants for violating civil law, not against the Public Works Department. The defendants are British and are under the jurisdiction of this court, so they should be sued here. He also said that when the court determines whether the Public Works Department has jointly violated civil law with the defendant, it can only be handled in accordance with British law, so the case should be heard by this court. Then, he cited similar cases as analogies.

Publishing World 149
