Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor, I recently read the "Local News" column in your newspaper on February 13, which contained a reader's advice regarding

Where Does China's Illness Lie? 154

丨丨Letter from Mr. Shen Zuguang丨

In your response to my article [Where Does China's Illness Lie?]: ㈠ I am most satisfied that you pointed out all the shortcomings in my article, giving me something to follow. ㈡ What I am not satisfied with is that the title is [Where Does China's Illness Lie?], yet it did not mention the source of the illness, leaving me without direction.

You seem to suspect that I am a remnant of the old regime, but that is not the case. I am a detached observer of society. The reason I proposed the article [Monarchy and Democracy] in my previous letter was because I was so dissatisfied with the current political reality. Because the federal system has not been implemented in China, we do not know if it is good or bad. Communism is also not suitable for the modern era. It seems that there are only two paths: monarchy and democracy. In fact, this question belongs to the realm of political science. There is no absolute good or bad in politics, so others cannot be prohibited from studying monarchy and democracy. Recently, for some reason, China's intellectual circles are most afraid of discussing monarchy, as if discussing monarchy is a heinous crime! In fact, modern civilized countries are either monarchies or democracies; one of the two must be the case. As you said: [Even in the French Republic, which has gone through hundreds of years of revolutionary struggle, there are still royalists]. Then we should not prohibit the study of monarchy and democracy simply because China was formerly a monarchy and is now a republic. Nor should you suspect that I have a relationship with the young emperor of the Qing Dynasty simply because I am discussing monarchy. In fact, if China were to assume a monarchy, who among the Chinese could not be emperor, but must recognize a thief as a father, leaving the throne vacant for Puyi to take? Wouldn't that be a joke? In modern monarchies and democracies, all citizens have the right to participate in politics. What the monarch gets is only a little administrative power. However, administrative power must still be approved by parliament. In addition, there is a parliament for legislation and judges for the judiciary. The monarch is just a nominal figure, just like the cabinet under the presidential system is responsible. Therefore, modern monarchs are different from the extremely autocratic ones who relied on divine right in the past. Many people now mistakenly believe that monarchs are not bound by the constitution established by the people and have supreme authority. In fact, this is not the case in modern monarchical states. Democracy can be said to be a suitable political system in the present era. However, under the current representative system, it can no longer satisfy people as it did fifty or sixty years ago. Therefore, many scholars of international law are studying the question of [which form of government is the most superior for civilized nations]. This also shows the future trend of the world.

You asked me [If you don't first explain what a nation is, how can you explain whether a nation is good or bad; if you don't first explain what a government is, how can you explain whether a government is good or bad?]. I thought we should talk about facts, not theory, so I didn't say what a nation and a government are. Now, in response to your question, I respectfully offer the following definition of a nation: [A common society of one or several ethnic groups, living in a fixed territory. Not ruled by external forces, to achieve common goals; and within it, there is an organized government, with guns to protect the entire population and make them obey]. This only explains one principle. There are several other principles to explain. If we go further and talk about the origin and origin of the nation, talk about the state system, political system, and ruling power, the story will be long. By government, we certainly do not mean the federal government, because China is not a federal country. We certainly do not mean the colonial government, because China is not a quasi-colonial country. We also do not mean the local government, because our target is the central government. Originally, by government, I meant the current party government in our country. In fact, there is more than one kind of nation. There are individualistic nations, socialist nations, and communist nations. We are only speaking abstractly. That is one point.

You said that I said: [The reason a nation exists is because of people, and the reason people exist is to live]. That's wrong! In fact, the occurrence of human groups is nothing more than survival competition. The current politics has deprived us of all the conditions for survival competition. Can we not cry bitterly? We believe that public affairs are too important to our overall interests and actions. Whether it is in life and property, association and assembly, speech and publication, if we do not have a good government, we will not be able to live and work in peace! So-called living in peace can also include life and property; so-called working happily can also include association, assembly, speech, and publication. That is the second point.

You asked me: [What exactly are the various systems you mentioned? Where exactly have they been tried?]. Before the first year of the Republic of China, the call for democracy in China was very high. As a result, after the change of era, democracy was implemented. Now, may I ask, where is the spirit of democracy? This is called a failed experiment! In the second year of the Republic, Yuan Shikai declared himself emperor, wanting to restore autocratic monarchy, but Cai Songpo started an uprising in Yunnan, and Yuan Shikai fell. This is called a failed experiment! The current Central Committee system imitates the organization of Soviet Russia, but loses its effectiveness. Because the political organization of Soviet Russia is very strict, and its leaders can concentrate their power and use it freely. But our country does not have his skills, and ends up neither in heaven nor on earth. This is called a failed experiment! That is the third point. You said: [We all came from the political reforms of 1898, the Eight-Nation Alliance, the Xinhai Revolution, and the Hongxian Emperor's dream]. Precisely because we came from them, we could not come up with anything new, so I am not satisfied! The Taiping Heavenly Kingdom's revolution had good motives! It is a pity that there was a lack of talent. Except for Qian Dongping and Shi Dakai, the rest were not worth mentioning. Therefore, it did not succeed. The Yihetuan's doctrine of supporting the Qing and destroying the foreigners was pitifully naive! So there were no results. When the Qing Dynasty was overthrown and the Republic of China was established, if China had someone like Ito Hirobumi to carry out reforms, China might have already been in good shape. However, the reformers at that time had conflicting opinions. When Sun Yat-sen resigned as interim president, all new plans vanished like clouds! Then came Yuan Shikai's declaration as emperor. To be honest, I have always believed in talent. You admitted that [the Yihetuan rose up to resist imperialism, giving the imperialists a head-on blow]. This is what I doubt? If the Yihetuan really gave the imperialists a head-on blow, then China would not have made a treaty under the city during the Eight-Nation Alliance! It is necessary to know that there are two elements to establishing a nation in the world: one is military force, and the other is diplomacy. Diplomacy and military force have a mutual relationship. Now, military force is not as good as others, and diplomacy is not as good as others. Instead of cultivating talents properly, we only know how to put up slogans saying: Down with imperialism! As a result, the three northeastern provinces were taken away by others! We sought help from the League of Nations, but the League of Nations did not help! We still do not realize our past mistakes until death. There is no saving us! That is the fourth point.

You said: [A group of ignorant people constantly talk about history, human feelings, customs, and habits! But I want to ask, what is history? What are human feelings? What are customs and habits?]. I respectfully answer as follows: History is a common principle, and also an abstract noun. In fact, the object of history is the total statistics of people, politics, and social changes. Which country in the world today does not base its civilization history on its own evolution and narrative? This is called not forgetting one's roots. Customs are also abstract nouns. It is not said: [What the superiors transform becomes custom, and what the inferiors transform becomes habit]. My meaning of customs is: [The beliefs and lifestyles transmitted and cultivated by an ethnic society]. For example, the Japanese sitting on the floor, the Indians worshiping Buddhism, the British and Americans using knives and forks instead of chopsticks, and the Chinese formerly performing kneeling ceremonies and now bowing, these are all customs. Human feelings and habits are also abstract nouns. So-called human feelings can be explained by the will in psychology; so-called habits can be explained by exercise in psychology. For example, the Japanese occupation of the three northeastern provinces is the will of the Japanese; that is, the human feelings of the Japanese. China's resistance to Japan is the will of the Chinese; that is also the human feelings of the Chinese. Also, for example, the Chinese working class is diligent and hardworking, which is a cultivated habit; the inhuman life of black slaves in the Americas is also a cultivated habit. (Their inhumanity should be considered an exception) You should not say that history, human feelings, customs, and habits are clichés. The bigger the question in the universe, the more abstract the noun. It is clear that there are individualistic nations, socialist nations, and communist nations, but recently there is a party called the nationalist faction. What kind of nationalism does it refer to? Also, for example, the government authorities advocate long-term resistance. This is also swallowing dates whole! What year and month will the so-called long-term be? What kind of strategy will the so-called resistance use? These are all vague nouns. It is enough to seek rationality for vague nouns in logic. Abstract and concrete, analysis and generalization, seem to be irrelevant. That is the fifth point.

You asked me: [How exactly do you prepare? What is the so-called preparation?]. When Turkey was about to perish, Kemal emerged, convened the National Salvation Congress, produced methods to save the nation, immediately sent troops, drove back the troops of various countries stationed in Turkish territory, and restored Turkey's national fortune. This is what I mean by [prepare and you will succeed]. The government repeatedly says it will resist Japan, but it does not resist Japan. It repeatedly says it will prepare, but it never prepares. This is what I mean by [if you do not prepare, you will fail]. In fact, saying determination, saying preparation, but still no determination, no preparation, is because in reality there is still no preparation, no solution. That is the sixth point.

In short, what I said in my previous letter was really out of dissatisfaction with the current political reality. I still ask you to tell me where China's illness lies? What medicine should be used to cure it? (The letter will be published tomorrow)

To Mr. Haizi: I have received your letter. Please speak with Mr. Yang at 364 Nanjing Road, Dalu Commercial Plaza. This is an announcement. Educational news headlines

Jiangxi Department of Education Holds Winter Vacation Training Program 156

Passed the Education Sector Covenant

The Jiangxi Department of Education, in order to utilize the winter vacation to assist educational personnel in continuing their studies, held an educational training program from February 4th to 10th, inviting experts to give lectures and hold various discussion sessions after the lectures. All lectures and discussions focused on national crisis education, production education, and personality education. The attendees were divided into designated and voluntary, totaling more than 350 people. The opening ceremony was held on the morning of the 4th, with Jiangxi Chairman Xiong Shihui lecturing on the national crisis and education. In the afternoon, Director Cheng Shiwei reported on the direction of educational administration. On the morning of the 6th, Xu Qingyu lectured on the meaning and realization of personality education, and Wang Zhenxin lectured on education and rural areas. In the afternoon, Wen Qun lectured on the rural cooperative movement. On the 7th, Director Cheng of the Department of Education lectured on the self-cultivation of educators and discussed the issue of national crisis education, deciding that the Department of Education would organize a National Crisis Education Research Association, refer to the discussion opinions, formulate a National Crisis Education Implementation Plan, and issue it to all schools for implementation. In the afternoon, the issue of personality education was discussed, and the attendees passed the fifteen articles of the Education Sector Covenant, and sent a letter requesting all educational personnel in the province to join in and abide by them. The original text of the covenant is attached below. (Education Sector Covenant) ㈠ Vow to wipe out national shame, ㈡ Use domestic goods, ㈢ Be punctual, ㈣ Do not gamble, ㈤ Vigorously abstain from smoking and alcohol, ㈥ Do not engage in unnecessary socializing (strive for frugality in wedding, funeral, and celebratory ceremonies, and limit gifts to a maximum of one yuan), ㈦ Vigorously eliminate factionalism, ㈧ Do not be greedy, ㈨ Always keep one's word, ㈩ Advocate courtesy and humility, ⑾ ㈠ Emphasize responsibility and de-emphasize rights, ⑾ ㈡ Be strict with oneself and lenient with others, ⑾ ㈢ Engage in labor that benefits both body and mind, ⑾ ㈣ Use a spirit of hard work and endurance to overcome all difficulties, ⑾ ㈤ Must spend at least one or two hours a day reading after work. The above is the situation of the first three days of the meeting. After the 8th, the lectures were all about production education, mostly lectured by Zhong Daozan, a supervisor of the Ministry of Education.

Local News

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Private Secondary Schools to Stop Enrolling Normal School Students 157

Starting from Autumn 1933

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed the private secondary schools in the city, saying, "It has been found that senior secondary schools concurrently offering normal school courses were originally intended to cultivate teachers, but in recent years, private secondary schools in the city have often concurrently offered normal school courses, only to cater to the psychology of some students, without regard to their facilities. The bureau has held several registrations of primary school teachers in the city, and the statistics have reached more than 3,500 people. Therefore, the city's primary school teachers are, in fact, in surplus. Recently, Article 4 of the Law on Normal Schools promulgated by the National Government states, [Normal schools shall be established by provinces or cities directly under the Executive Yuan, but may also be established by counties or cities or jointly by two or more counties according to local needs]. According to this provision, normal schools should be public and not attached to secondary schools as a principle. Most of the private secondary schools in the city that concurrently offer normal school courses are simple and their facilities are not perfect. They should be reorganized as soon as possible. All private secondary schools in the city that concurrently operate normal school courses shall not recruit new students from the academic year of 1933 (i.e., from the autumn of 1933). Old students will continue until graduation. This has been decided by the 252nd bureau affairs meeting of the bureau on January 10th of this year, and the Ministry of Education has issued Instruction No. 978 on January 20th, approving the proposed handling. This order is hereby issued for your information." This order.

Overview of School Education and Social Education

According to the statistics of public and private entertainment venues in the city in January of this year, there is the following table:

Now, I will specifically discuss the two most common and important items, [Entertainment.

㈠ Regarding movies: Because Shanghai is the center of China's film industry and the largest market for foreign films in China, movies in this city have a more significant meaning for social education. The city has an organization called the Film Censorship Committee, which strictly examines all films. Regardless of Chinese or Western films, any that are harmful to social morality are either completely prohibited or partially censored, so as not to harm society. This work has been quite effective. Although it is now handled uniformly by the central government, the city authorities still strictly inspect films at any time according to orders, so that films can show a good response in social education, and absolutely prohibit the screening of all improper films that are harmful to social customs. We know that the Public Concession Board also has a film censorship organization, but I hope that they will fully cooperate with the municipal government and, under the guidance of the central government, crack down on bad films.

㈡ Regarding operas and records: Similarly, as with films, the Municipal Education Bureau has an Opera and Record Review Committee, which is responsible for strictly reviewing operas and records.

In addition, the Municipal Education Bureau pays considerable attention to all entertainment venues and advocates strictly prohibiting all harmful entertainment. This work is inherently biased towards the negative, but at the same time, there are considerable plans on the positive side. Because of the short time, I won't say much more here.

In short, what I have said here is all based on facts. Since the establishment of the Municipal Government, it has not been long, so all work, it can be said frankly, is still in the initial stage of construction. Although we are actively moving forward and are unwilling to make do, because of the actual difficulties, we are still very, very far from our assumed goals. Fortunately, the plan has been determined and we are more determined to build. We dare to believe that, as long as a considerable amount of time passes, the city's achievements in education will be more positive and more widespread.

I have roughly finished talking about the overview of school education and social education in the city. Originally, I could have finished my speech. However, now is still a time of national crisis, a very critical time. Just talking about Shanghai in terms of Shanghai, and talking about education in terms of education, we in Shanghai's education sector still feel the impact of the Japanese invasion of Songhu very strongly. All the losses are not easy to recover for a while. We only need to check the number of war losses reported by public and private schools in Shanghai to understand the extent of the impact. According to the reports received by the Municipal Education Bureau, they are as follows:

Level Number of Schools Amount of Loss (Silver)

Primary Schools 81 280,867 yuan

Secondary Schools 31 1,893,586 yuan

Higher Education Institutions 17 8,716,508 yuan

Total 129 10,890,961 yuan

When you enter school, it is not only to prepare for going to university in the future, but more importantly, to prepare for how to be a person in the future. We hope that you will be modern female citizens, not fashionable college students. However, being a modern female citizen entails responsibilities no less than those of men, and sometimes even greater. Because if China has a good woman, she can educate several good children, which is of great importance to the nation. Therefore, on the one hand, we should seek the cultivation of knowledge, and on the other hand, we should have a deep observation of things in order to lead and educate children. Then, the new Director of Academic Affairs, Ms. Duan Ying, reported on the school's policy for this semester.

Dazhong Middle School: Dazhong Middle School on Jessfield Road is known for its excellent teachers and strict management. This semester, the number of new students enrolling and those transferring from other schools has been very enthusiastic. The school is scheduled to start classes this week and still has vacancies to accommodate new students. They are currently busy adding all kinds of equipment. It is also heard that the library and laboratory will be greatly expanded this semester. Yesterday afternoon, Principal Zhi Rang hosted a dinner for all faculty and staff at the Bankers' Association to discuss plans for this semester.

Wuxi Native Association Night School: The Wuxi Native Association in Shanghai has been running an evening school at No. 278 Qipu Road for five years to facilitate supplementary studies for the younger brothers of fellow villagers and store employees, teaching practical knowledge for business and life. The school specializes in three subjects: Chinese, English, and arithmetic, and does not charge tuition fees. Anyone with a primary school education of two or three years or above, regardless of age, can go for supplementary studies. Classes have already started on the 10th. It is heard that there are still vacancies. Those who wish to study there can be recommended by store managers or members.

Minzhi Journalism College: Minzhi Journalism College, a specialized school at No. 1413 Xiafei Road in this city, will officially start classes on the 16th. Classes are held daily from 5:30 pm to 8:30 pm, which is the same as the method used by Soochow University Law School, making it convenient for students who have jobs or are studying at other universities. In terms of curriculum, Mr. Zhou Changqing, a graduate of the Social Science Department of Moscow Sun Yat-sen University, will teach Russian; Mr. Fang Tianpei, a Master of Arts from Columbia University in the United States, will teach English; Mr. Zhang Xianmei, an engineer from the "Xinwenbao" newspaper, will teach newspaper engineering; photographer Mr. Yang Xiuming will teach photography; and Mr. Gu Zhizhong, executive director of the "Xinwenbao" interviewing department, will teach journalism and comparative constitutional law. The school still has vacancies.

Lide Elementary School: Lide Elementary School on Connaught Road and Xiaoshadu Road in this city has been established for more than two years. Principal Xu Lide (also known as Xingchu) is enthusiastic about school affairs and has achieved considerable success. There are currently two campuses with about 200 students. Yesterday morning, a memorial week for Sun Yat-sen was held, and Mr. Xu Zeyi was invited to give a lecture. The ceremony was conducted as scheduled. First, Principal Xu reported, and then Mr. Xu lectured on the story of model children.

Nanyang Wireless Telegraph Training Institute: The Nanyang Wireless Telegraph Training Institute on Route Tenant de Bayle in the French Concession was jointly established by alumni of Nanyang University. It was established early and has achieved remarkable results. Graduates of the school serve in various telecommunications agencies in the country. Several dozen radio operators at the Shanghai Ministry of Communications radio station are graduates of the school. The seventh class of students, including Shen Tingming and 13 others, have graduated and have been introduced by the school to serve in the Signal Corps of the Ministry of Military Affairs. This class has already started recruiting. In view of the development of wireless telephone services, in addition to the radio operation courses, an engineering course has been opened. There has been an enthusiastic response from those who have applied.

The Shanghai Job Placement Center was entrusted by a certain organization in this city yesterday to introduce two or three general affairs staff, specializing in printing miscellaneous work and serving as errand runners, somewhere between workers and junior staff. Applicants must be between 15 and 18 years old, from poor families, and able to endure hardship. Board and lodging are provided, and pocket money is given. Spring and Autumn

Flattery and the Kick 175

— Zhanlu

In this era where "flattery can get you anywhere," flattering people and living day by day are certainly the tricks of a clown. But! If flattery is not done properly, it can be like the saying: "Flattering people only to get a kick in the pants," then it becomes "doing good only to become bad."

Who does good only to become bad? Please look at a Persian reporter.

Recently, according to a telegram from the Persian capital: a reporter from the Kotchishi newspaper in the Persian capital, in order to praise the wisdom of the Persian king for dismissing the chief attendant, Di Muschi, wrote an article praising the Persian king to the best of his ability. Who knew that he had angered the Persian king and was sentenced to disrespect and great disrespect, and ordered to work as a street cleaner in front of the palace as a slight warning. The Persian king was still considered civilized and did not execute the reporter in a muddle-headed way. However, it is also extremely ridiculous for a great reporter to become a street cleaner and practice "intellectuals swept from the earth."

Having lost the clumsy pole, and clinging to this street-cleaning broom, both are using effort under the wrist, but the upper-level work has become lower-level work. Can you still "sweep thousands of people with a clumsy tip"? Most Chinese reporters are accustomed to using writing brushes, so when they become street cleaners, they can only hold a reed broom. Foreign reporters do not use writing brushes but fountain pens, so this reporter from the Kotchishi newspaper can only hold a wire broom! If it is a day for a big cleanup, he can be hired as an instructor! Hehe!

Spring Snow 176

— Xiangdi

Getting up in the morning, I suddenly saw pure white snow piled on the houses, and I felt quite surprised in my heart; last night was not very cold, yet it had snowed, and how could I not have known at all?

The old calendar is already the Lantern Festival, and time has finally crept into spring. Naturally, the snow that fell last night was spring snow. It is said that spring snow melts more easily than winter snow, and indeed it is true. The snow that accumulated last night had completely melted before noon, leaving almost no trace.

Although spring snow is not as interesting as winter snow, it is not something that spoils the scenery. Winter snow adorning plum blossoms is more poetic, and spring snow adorning peach blossoms or...

Japanese cherry blossoms, I think, would be even more poetic. It's a pity that in the second or third month of spring when peach blossoms or cherry blossoms are in full bloom, it rarely snows in spring, which is truly a scene-spoiler.

I remember that Japan seems to have more snow than China. I have seen spring snow once or twice, and it happened to be when the cherry blossoms were just blooming. Once, I also invited a few friends who loved to see cherry blossoms to Ueno Shrine to see the cherry blossoms after the snow, then we played in Ueno Park, and then took the tram to see them at Asukayama. Unfortunately, I couldn't write poetry, so although I had poetic feelings, I didn't create a poem; only one Japanese female classmate who could compose haiku made a very beautiful haiku. Recalling these elegant events now, they are like a light dream, floating and disappearing.

In China, especially in bustling and unbearably vulgar cities like Shanghai, even peach blossoms are rarely seen. Even if it snows in February or March, it's useless. It's better not to come down so reluctantly. Poetic feeling will never exist here, I think.

To Dalian 177

— Juan Yun

I cannot forget that [Dalian] is our Chinese land, a part forcibly occupied by Japanese power; it is the source of the invasion of Manchuria and Mongolia by Japanese ambitious figures! It's no exaggeration, they have already become obedient subjects under Japanese rule. Anyone living in Dalian can no longer imagine that [Dalian] was once Chinese territory! Disgraced warlords, treacherous merchants who monopolize Japanese goods, people who can no longer gain a foothold in mainland China, there is no better way than to go to Dalian.

[Refugees and Traitors] Dalian is a sanctuary for this group of people. Wealthy Chinese people, seeing the chaos in the country, going abroad to foreign countries seems too troublesome, might as well buy a house in Dalian and become a carefree [Dalian recluse]!

I have been to Dalian a total of four times. The first three times were from Tianjin, taking the Tangshan Maru back to Qingdao, passing through Dalian. It required a delay of two days.

The most recent time was last year in July, after recovering from illness in Beiping for three weeks. I decided to take a trip to Harbin via Dalian. At least through my work, I could observe the secrets along the way of the Manchurian puppet state.

This time going to Dalian was not as free as before. Upon arriving at the pier, I had to sign my name and write a detailed statement stating where I was going and the specific reasons for my business.

It was really difficult, although I had many friends living under the Manchurian puppet state, but my purpose and business, even I myself had not decided. In order to fulfill the formalities, I had to mention Mr. X, who lives in Dalian.

Mr. X received me very warmly, and the reunion after a long separation seemed especially polite. During our private talks, we talked about the affairs of the Manchurian puppet state.

Truly conscienceless! There are actually Chinese people bringing money to invest in Manchuria! At the same time, I can well remember that during the January 28th Shanghai Incident last year, there were even people advocating expanding trade with Japan!

Danger and obstacles, after I lingered in Dalian for three days, Mr. X strongly discouraged my trip to Harbin.

Delighted Hope for Clouds and Rainbows 178

— ·Ti·Gong

Before Eyun came, Yifen repeatedly praised her beauty. When Eyun was about to come, the fellow member Xu Ziquan praised her art even more. Mr. Ziquan, some say he has a suggestive relationship with her, but his words may not be entirely trustworthy. Comparing her first night's performance, it was indeed flawless.

From behind the curtain, a sound of "bitter ah" revealed a talented person. Her appearance is beautiful, her voice is sweet, and her performance of the Erhuang aria follows the style of Tan Xinpei, pleasing to the ears. The facial expressions are just right. It's a pity that her starry eyes are slightly small, failing to fully convey the spirit. Her stage steps, preferring to touch the ground with her toes, slightly detract from the beauty. Considering her singing and acting as a whole, she is sufficient to surpass others and compete with Xue Yanqun.

Singing "E Yun Xing," she is worthy of her name, and the people of Shanghai looking forward to her beauty is like a great drought hoping for clouds and rainbows. Therefore, I offer the four words "Delighted Hope for Clouds and Rainbows" as a gift to her.

A Glimpse of the Tea Dance 179

— Guo Lanxin

In the midst of flying rain and snow, it really seemed as if I saw refugees from the Northeast, crying out in hunger and cold. I and Jin Yu, in order to fulfill a bit of our wish to help our compatriots in the Northeast, endorsed several tickets, and also braved the rain and snow to attend. The time of arrival was half past five. The Rue Lafayette in the rain and snow had a different kind of flavor.

Arriving outside the gate of the Amusement Park, I saw the party and national flags hanging as if in tears. We went in and saw cars displayed like an exposition, knowing that many people had attended. At the same time, it was also clear that many of the attendees were from the bourgeoisie, who should donate some money and also be able to spend money to save the country and help their compatriots.

We went upstairs, and there were still many people continuing to come, but regrettably it was already full. We went up another floor to observe, looking down into the dance hall below, filled with many party and national dignitaries, famous figures out of office, social celebrities, their wives and daughters, and star dancers. The fragrance of clothes, the shape of beards, the brilliance of pearls and jewelry, there was no shadow of refugees, only a display of vying for beauty, flaunting and exaggerating.

I thought to myself that if the decorations of the wives, daughters, and stars present could be donated, the value would exceed the ticket income by hundreds of times, and the refugees in the Northeast would surely benefit greatly. But this is just my own thought; in reality, it will never be realized.

Because there were no seats, we toured around, seeing many novel and magnificent fashions. Those clothing materials were all Western goods. At the same time, I felt that the cost of the perms, powder, rouge, lipstick, and perfume of the women who participated this time would also be enough to account for several fractions of the total ticket income, right? How grand!

Finally, after staying for five minutes, we began to leave. The music of the waltz sent us off. Joy, embraces, wild dancing, refugees, iron and blood, the illusion of national subjugation seemed to be intertwined and spinning. We had no intention of staying, so we rushed out of the glass door, jumped into the car, and returned. At the same time, cars were still carrying groups of people in. The rain and snow were flying up at this time, like tears of despair.

Novel

The Strange Encounter of the Novel "Hun Jianglong" (River-stirring Dragon) 180

— Huo Xueming

The river was very wide, very clear, and bottomless, just a distant expanse of clear blue, a layer of flowing mercury-like shimmering moonlight. But River-stirring Dragon's experience would not fail because of this. He could find the trace-free [fish nests]. Soon, at a withered tree where the water swirled unusually, on the waves where the shadow slanted, he gained endless hope. A desire like wildfire raised its head and repeatedly teased the fragile branches of the reeds, habitually jumping over here. He quickly took off his outer cotton-padded jacket.

In less than the blink of an eye, he straightened his legs, moved the fishing spear, and made a pose like a squirrel, using all his strength. He looked closely, and then jumped into the water.

A huge splash of water jumped up, startling the crows roosting on the large elm tree, and causing them to fly and cry in all directions. The狂響 barking of dogs echoed from nearby villages, and the reeds sighed as if...... Without saying, patterns like swirls immediately appeared on the river surface, like a shattered white crystal mirror of moonlight.

Here, the fishing spear tightly gripped in River-stirring Dragon's hand had deeply pierced into the river bottom, and his entire body was submerged in the cold water. As usual, his multi-pronged fishing spear would find three or five crucian carp or blackfish. The cost of his effort would definitely not be too bad, he was very clear. So, he grasped the handle of the fishing spear with both hands underwater, and pulled it up with force. It was very heavy, definitely a big fish. He thought: as usual, he could conveniently hide them one by one in his fish basket. At this time, the air around Lingjia River returned to silence and cold.

[What?] River-stirring Dragon began to utter this surprised scream in the water. The water surface was silent. He immediately surfaced and jumped towards the shore, opening his eyes to see that a bloody little child's head was hanging on the tip of the fishing spear, shockingly. Under the moonlight, it could be seen that this head belonged to his own newborn baby. (3)

Each Has Its Merits

Introduction 181

My friends, there are many who can write well, and there are also many who don't write much but write very well. For example, my old friend Ding Song, he has always been known as [Ximen Qing exhausted his fame in his time, acquiring a good hand in painting], but his articles are not easy to read. This time, I had a whimsical idea, so I specially invited these friends who don't write much to write some articles for us to read, just like a famous actor performing a reversed role on stage. I generally call it [Each Has Its Merits.]

Shou Juan

Lying on a Board Door (Part 1) 182

— Ding Song

Teacher ××:

Because I drift everywhere, and my whereabouts are uncertain, I can't even tell you a mailing address, so naturally I hope to receive your reply, but in fact, it will never happen. However, the two letters I sent you before should not be lost by the post office, right?

Teacher! Now I think that a person's luck cannot be forced. Thanks to the kindness of the teacher and teacher's wife, who helped me step into the door of society, I extremely wanted to do my best and create some great achievements. Firstly, to repay my loving mother's hardship in raising me, and secondly, to live up to the expectations of the teachers. But time has passed like lightning, and not only have my hopes of achieving a career become a bubble, but I am afraid that there will be a danger that I will not be able to meet you in the future! Thinking about it now, I feel indescribably uncomfortable! Putting everyone's kindness completely to waste, the more I think about it, the more heartbroken I am, the more I think about it, the more annoyed I am! Now my nerves are receiving extremely intense stimulation. If I didn't have a loving mother alive, I would have killed myself long ago!

Teacher, don't think that I am groaning without illness. Thinking about it, I really have many things to apologize to you all!·····························

This is a letter that a very proud female student of Mr. S sent him from 　埠. After reading it, he felt very unhappy. He thought that her family only had an old mother and two elder sisters, and both elder sisters were widows and addicted to opium. Within the family, there were no uncles or brothers, and all living expenses depended entirely on this weak woman who was not yet twenty years old, who had to compete and struggle for survival in this man-eating society. This was an extremely pitiful thing. But looking at the tone of her letter, it seemed to contain a kind of unspeakable secret, which really made him have ten thousand doubts.

One day eight years ago, on an old lunar New Year's Day, in the厢房 side room of a 石库门 shikumen-style house in 里 Lane on ×× Road, there was a board door placed there. Lying on the board door was a corpse, covered from head to toe with a semi-new, semi-old printed silk padded quilt. It was impossible to tell whether it was male or female, but the corpse's abdomen was bulging, which was a bit odd. Next to it was an old woman with already gray hair, and two middle-aged women crying, all folding paper ingots in their hands, the scene was very tragic. After a while, suddenly they heard the sound of the gate, and a few people walked in. The first to enter was a middle-aged man, wearing a very neat Western suit, with a very solemn attitude. Three women followed behind, all dressed very neatly. One was a twenty-something round-faced woman with a tall figure and a very delicate appearance; one was about thirty years old, and her appearance was not bad; one was a little older, with a plump figure and a good complexion. As they walked in, the two women in the side room, seeing them, immediately put down the folded paper ingots in their hands with tears and rushed forward to greet them. The old woman also came forward to greet them. When they walked to the board door where the corpse was placed, they gently lifted the end of the padded quilt covering the corpse with their hands. It revealed a young female corpse with yellow complexion like wax, and a head full of hair.

Business Sutra

Basic Conditions When Buying Woolen Fabrics 193

Woolen fabrics have varying selling prices and the quality of the material varies greatly. The key is whether they are pure wool or wool-cotton blends. If it is a wool-cotton blend, what is the proportion of artificial fiber and yarn? Identifying these aspects will help you understand the quality of the woolen fabric. But how can you tell if it is all wool or a wool-cotton blend? There is no other method because precise testing requires equipment, which is not possible when buying goods in a hurry. The only thing you can do is a general observation. (1) Take the entire sample and rub it vigorously with both hands. When you release it, if there are no wrinkles, it is undoubtedly made of all wool (because wool yarn has elasticity and stretches when released). (2) Take several warp and weft threads from the woolen fabric in both horizontal and vertical directions and burn them. There will be an unpleasant odor, and the curl will shrink very quickly. Because wool has oil, it makes a slight squeaking sound, and the dark gray ash condenses like beads. If it is yarn, there is no unpleasant odor, the ash is easily scattered because it has no oil, and it burns when it encounters fire, unlike wool yarn, which burns quickly. Secondly, you must decide what you want to buy and not listen to the store clerk. Store clerks want to be loyal to their duties and will only consider the interests of the store and will not consider the interests of the customer. Therefore, discussing with the store clerk what kind of material to buy is no different from "asking a fox for its skin" (seeking advice from an untrustworthy source). So, make your own decision in advance and ask the store clerk for advice when you go to the store, only for reference. The most wasteful thing is (1) not knowing the quality of the material, but only listening to the price. After looking at the sample, only ask the price and keep asking for more samples to see. The store clerk's opportunity has come. He turns around a few times in the storage room or at the tree window, takes the same quality material, and quotes a high price. Or he picks out the one with the best profit in the store and shakes it out to you. Then you have been fooled. So, when buying material, first, determine how much money per foot you are willing to spend. Second, ask the store clerk for a few samples to look at in order to compare the fabric and calculate the price. Don't think that "the high price is the good product." So, if you don't know how to buy, it's better to go to a woolen fabric shop with non-negotiable prices. If you know how to bargain and are buying ordinary woolen fabrics, it is more convenient to go to the Quan Pan Street area because there are many shops to compare and you can bargain for about 30 cents. If you are buying high-end clothing materials, it is best to go to woolen fabric shops in the Outer Bridge area, because all the Western clothing stores in the city get their goods from them (showing samples to the Western clothing stores). Therefore, the quality of the woolen fabric is good. However, they mostly only sell double widths (imported woolen fabrics are originally double width for the convenience of making Chinese clothes, so they are cut in half into single widths, without a width). When buying, it is best to buy with a partner, which is the same as each buying a single width. When discussing the price, it is better to specify the price per unit than per foot. For example, if you want to cut a robe from a double-width material and two people buy it together, cutting 5 yards is enough. Using feet, it is 9.5 feet. Nowadays, most people use city feet. Store clerks use "flying feet" (exaggerated measurements), which seems like a lot, but it is still the same. Using yardsticks has fewer drawbacks. However, one thing is that the yardstick must be a Deke yardstick (2.6 feet, used when Zhan Zhong imports goods). If you use their own-made yardstick, it is only 2.5 feet. In other words, woolen fabric shops also have two kinds of yardsticks, one for importing goods and one for selling goods. In this import and export, they have already taken one inch from each yard. If we customers also ask him to use the Deke yardstick, he will be less likely to profit.

Wheat Futures Market Turns Bullish 194

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was extremely quiet in the morning, with only the July contract opening a few times. The rest of the months were auctioned off empty. When the afternoon session opened, although trading was not much, the market atmosphere seemed lively. Because the foreign wheat quotation was slightly better, hedging was watching and hesitant, and off-market short sellers covered their positions more, so the asking price was high. However, in reality, there is very little basis for this situation to rise. As a result, the current month was better than the previous week by 1 fen, March was better by 2 fen, April was better by 3 fen, and July was better by 2 fen.

Chicago Wheat Slightly Firmer 195

(Eleventh) Chicago wheat rose due to strong Winnipeg wheat and poor winter production. Also, 10 million bushels were traded on the 10th. The market conditions for the 11th are listed below:

Sugar Market Affected by New Scale Dispute 196

Yesterday, the sugar market was stable due to firm tender prices. However, public association clearing transactions were unusually sluggish, with only asking prices and very few transactions. It is also heard that the local South Goods industry has a firm intention to temporarily suspend imports before the new scale problem is resolved. Therefore, the market is even quieter. The asking price for 24 coarse white sugar was 15.7 liang, and for high-quality goods, it was 8 qian. The asking price for No. 20 and No. 18 medium white sugar was 15.3 to 15.4 qian, and for No. 890 Dutch red sugar, it was 12.3 to 12.4 qian. There were few domestic green, red, and white sugar and Jianbing (rock sugar) offerings. The sluggishness of the market is unprecedented.

The Market Price of Quanzhou's Big Bubble Longan, Sold at the North Gate, Diverges from its Origin 197

Quanzhou's Big Bubble Longan, in past years, has always had a turning point during the New Year's red plate. This year's first round, in addition to the slightly higher prices for medium and lower grades, the rest of the grades have not opened up at the original price, showing a tired sign. However, according to the local situation, a divergent situation has formed. The Hua Ping ship only arrived with 327 boxes, and according to a letter, the local price has risen by 2 to 3 yuan. This is because the harvest last year was too abundant, and the branches and leaves were scorched, and some had even withered. In addition, heavy frost fell, and buds have not yet sprouted. According to general observation, this year's harvest will definitely be poor. Therefore, the owners of the goods are all hoping for higher prices and are unwilling to sell cheaply. However, local sales in Shanghai have not been smooth, making it difficult to improve for a while.

Oil Market - Asphalt Soars 198

Last Year, Various Regions Reported a Shortage; Zhejiang Route Production Area Purchased From Outside

Last year, various regions reported a shortage of asphalt. At the end of the market, there was no inventory in Hankou, Shanghai, and Hangzhou. It was generally expected that the spring market would inevitably rise. The Zhejiang route took the lead, and Hangzhou merchants went out to purchase goods, starting from Jiaxing, Zhejiang West, and then to Shanghai and Hankou. It is estimated that about 1,000 pieces were purchased from Jiaxing, starting from 27 to 28 yuan per dan to 32 to 33 yuan. Shanghai also had 1,000 pieces of heavy hemp, starting from 18 liang to 20 liang. Macheng started from 17 liang to 19 liang. About 6,000 to 7,000 pieces were purchased in Hankou, with heavy hemp from 15.6 liang to 18 liang, and Macheng from 13 liang to 16 liang. In total, Hangzhou merchants purchased about 10,000 pieces abroad within half a month. As the Zhejiang route is originally an oil-producing area, the fact that they are now purchasing from outside indicates that the production area has been greatly reduced. Given that the Zhejiang route only has the source of Hankou, and Hangzhou, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Ningbo, and the local area all purchase from Hankou, the Hankou market has become chaotic and prices have risen chaotically. Also, at the time when the inventory at the end of the year was extremely thin, the source of supply was blocked by ice and snow. Whenever goods arrived, there was a scramble to buy them, regardless of the price, but only seeking the goods. The goods along the way were sold out before they even arrived. According to the details in yesterday's Hankou letter, 1,500 to 1,600 pieces of heavy hemp and 2,000 pieces of Macheng have been confirmed but not delivered. A large number have not been purchased. Currently, transactions are temporarily suspended, and sales will resume only after the confirmed purchases have been cleared and there are surplus goods. As the amount of goods in transit and the date of arrival cannot be determined, merchants are afraid to sell them in advance. It is estimated that heavy hemp will have to be delivered at 19 liang or more. Recently, only a small number of Pianfeng Macheng have been offered at a price of 17 liang. Subsequent goods were priced at 17.4 liang, while previous goods were generally priced at 18 liang. However, as various regions see that there is no spot oil to buy in Hankou, even with daily letters and telegrams urging purchases, there is no effect and they can only wait quietly.

Silk, Tea, and Rayon Selling Well, Market Firm 199

Recently, the spring silk selling season has arrived, and the demand for rayon from various silk weaving factories in the interior has increased sharply, with sales reaching smoothly. Yesterday, silk merchants from Hangzhou and Huzhou in the public association again imported 47 boxes of current and forward goods of medium and high-quality snow dragon and other brands of rayon from France and other countries at prices ranging from 132.75 to 147.5 liang. The market plate is increasingly showing a firm appearance.

O-Mei Silk (European and American) Telegram Transfer to Shanghai Awaits 200

Yesterday, the foreign firm silk market in the local port was calm and flat. This was because the telegrams of period and spot silk sent to overseas countries by various European and American firms still needed time to be transferred. Various European firms, in view of the silk thread factories in New York and Lyon, purchased their raw materials as needed, and the price of period silk was not much different from the price of spot silk. Therefore, general hoarders held the view that they would not buy the period silk unless it was cheap. Chinese silk merchants had high costs and large losses, and maintained their stance as before. The market atmosphere was calm.

Hardware, Overseas Tinplate Continues to Rise 201

Recently, hardware and various goods have seen frequent transactions due to the economic situation and the purchase of Jinling and Hanyang military factories in Shanghai. Among them, military supplies are the most, such as white lead skin, black iron skin, tinplate, triangular iron, new lead wire, etc. There is also some embellishment for water cement and refined spirits. Therefore, the market situation is good. However, there were very few transactions by customer groups and construction groups yesterday, due to the influence of late money shop loans. The market conditions, on the other hand, saw more increases than decreases. For example, half-fen 7.5-li steel plates rose another 2.5 qian, with half-fen estimated at 6.75 liang, and 7.5-li at 6.5 liang. Tinplate also rose by 2 to 3 qian. The estimated price of 90-pound British goods was 13.1 liang, 100-pound was 13.75 liang, 90-pound American goods were 14.9 liang, 100-pound was 16 liang, and 200-pound Huisi iron was 26 liang. However, there were not many goods on the market, and after the price increase, the standard may rise again. Other items, such as Qing lead, also turned up 1 qian, estimated at 12 liang, and 26-gauge British white iron also rose to 12 liang. The estimated price of No. 2 white lead skin was 27.25 liang. As for the price decreases, only a few items such as Dian Xi (spot tin) were seen. However, according to overseas telegraphic communications yesterday, the price of tinplate continued to rise by 2 to 3 shillings, with the price of 90-pound boxes estimated at 17 shillings 5 pence, 100-pound boxes at 18 shillings 2 pence, 180-pound boxes at 1 pound 16 shillings 2 pence, 160-pound boxes at 1 pound 15 shillings 9 pence, and 200-pound boxes at 1 pound 18 shillings. It is heard that those in the same industry are afraid to start adding orders because their market conditions are rising too fast. Therefore, in recent days, apart from inquiries, there have been no actual transactions.

Free Talk

Dragon Lanterns 224

— Sha Tuo

Although it’s close to spring, outside the window it's still wind and snow. I sit in the upstairs room, surrounded by a desolate silence, thinking of the scene of the first month in the mountains; as usual, these few days are for the dragon lantern procession.

In the mountains, performing the dragon lantern procession is not a simple matter. Not only is it just once a year, but it is also the only outdoor competition for the strong young men of the mountains. The city has dragon boat races in May, but the mountains have nothing like that.

From the day before the Lantern Festival until the seventeenth, people from far and near wear their brand new spring clothes and rush to the town for the dragon procession. No matter how far they come from, they don't have to worry about food and lodging. Those with relatives naturally go to their relatives’ homes for New Year's greetings, and even strangers or passersby without relatives will be welcomed with smiling faces. During these four days, every household in the town has an obligation to provide food and lodging, and the more generous the hospitality, the better. After dinner, as the lanterns are about to be lit, the streets are already packed with people, the old leaning on chairs, the young jumping around, and the girls with their braids shyly avoiding the gazes of strangers. Regardless of whether it's sunny or rainy, cold or warm, everyone is equally happy. If the blue sky is like a wash, and the round moon is overhead, that would naturally be even better. In addition to the lantern light and the shadows of people, adding the moonlight like water, everyone becomes even more enthusiastic.

While waiting quietly, the sound of gongs and drums comes from far to near. The cloth dragon, more than twenty yards long, passes by with its teeth and claws bared. Everyone doesn't just scatter after one look, as the best part is yet to come. Those with houses sit by the windows to watch, those without houses crowd to the village entrance to see the dragon cross the creek. One dragon dances on the bridge, and another dragon swims underwater. The lantern light makes the creek water glow red, a bit dazzling. After crossing the creek, the dragon crawls into the mysterious and dark forest. The lantern light flickers uncertainly among the branches and leaves, and after a while, it winds around behind the mountain.

The grandmother tells her daughter-in-law to make more tea, the guests from the bottom of the mountain munch on pumpkin seeds freshly brought from the county seat, the older children set off firecrackers, and the younger children clamor to sleep. The mother gently coaxes them: [Don't sleep, wait for the dragon to return, and it will bless you to grow quickly, to grow as tall as your father.]

The dragon is returning! The children sit on their parents' shoulders, looking up at the mountain ridge. At first, only a red glow rises, then a dragon's head appears, and sections of the dragon's belly emerge from the back of the mountain. The silent valley suddenly turns red like a wildfire. The mountain ridge is winding, and the dragon follows the ridge as it crawls down, looking like lightning on a June night, or like a golden thread. After the dragon's tail is finished turning, the dragon's head is already halfway down the mountain. This is when the excitement starts, with firecrackers being set off in front of every house, and children and women all bowing down to the dragon, while the dogs throughout the village bark non-stop towards the mountain.

Afterwards, the dragon returns to the temple, and this is when everyone goes to sleep. Except for the head of the household, everyone can sleep until noon, preparing for the second and third nights of staying up.

The Lantern Festival is the happiest few days for the children, but also the most melancholic days. After the seventeenth, everyone has to take off their new clothes and start working.

Thinking of the joyous events in the mountains while in Shanghai, it’s not just the dragon procession. But in this flurry of spring snow, I wonder if the dragon procession is still being performed well on the old mountain ridge?

Illegal and Non-Illegal 225

— Yu Dafu

The China League for Civil Rights Protection established a branch in Beiping and spent a lot of effort to rescue many students who were arrested for resisting Japan and opposing imperialism. The Beiping Municipal Party Committee therefore suggested that it was an illegal organization.

Law, it seems, comes in many kinds. Near Shanghai, people often sell "Fuyang Law" [a type of local pastry], and throughout China, there are people who know a magic trick that everyone can learn. In the story of "San Niang Teaches Her Son," there is even a bamboo stick for beating children called "family law." These laws are what we are accustomed to. As for the law of the spirit of rule of law, the law of legislation and justice, we only see them in the names of various committees, on the signboards of government offices, and in newspaper orders. The true embodiment of the law, the just public trial, the judgment of right and wrong, seems to be rarely encountered in Chinese society and politics. In foreign paintings, the goddess of law has a cloth covering her eyes and is holding a balance in her hand. I think that if we were to paint this goddess in China, we could copy the foreign painting completely, but we would have to add some gun barrels or gold-made weights to the scales in her hand.

The several cases that the China League for Civil Rights Protection has recently been striving to oppose and assist with are well known to everyone: 1) the murder of Zhenjiang journalist Liu Yusheng; 2) the arrest of students and workers for resisting Japanese imperialist aggression; 3) the detention of political prisoners for fighting for political freedom of speech, publication, assembly, association, and demonstration, etc. To determine whether the League is illegal or non-illegal, we must first ask whether the things it opposes are illegal or non-illegal.

Therefore, we must ask: Was the murder of Liu Yusheng illegal or not? Is the Manchukuo a legitimate organization that we should all recognize and support? Should freedom of speech, publication, etc., be granted to the people in law?

China has reached a period full of crises. Everyone should wake up. Hiding in the corner and making trouble, are you really not afraid of the coming dawn?

A Chat About Longevity, From Ancient Times to the Present 226

— Li Shengyue

It's probably because Chinese emperors were too afraid of kicking the bucket that they always liked their subjects to call them [Long Live]. The two characters [Long Live] became the exclusive title of the emperor in successive dynasties, just as the character [朕] became the emperor's exclusive first person pronoun. In fact, [Long Live] was not necessarily a respectful term for the emperor in the beginning. Those who have read Han Feizi probably remember that [Long Live] was originally just a kind of congratulatory term used by shamans. The use of [Long Live] as a respectful term for the emperor probably began in the Han Dynasty. When Grand General Wei Zhen of Emperor Xian was awe-inspiring and famous, a group of officials in Chang'an prostrated themselves before him and called out [Long Live]. A good-for-nothing named Han Leng blushed and protested, saying, [Can ministers call each other [Long Live]?] It can be seen that at that time, [Long Live] was not something that could be shouted casually.

I often feel that the psychology of [Long Live] and the emperor's fear of death is extremely contradictory, because as soon as these two words are uttered, they are cursing the emperor that even if he lives to ten thousand years, he will still inevitably kick the bucket (die), just like congratulating a commoner's son on [living to be a hundred years old], which contains the same malicious curse. A commoner's life is worthless, and living to a hundred years is considered long life. Compared to the emperor's ten thousand years, it is indeed like the cicada or mayfly that does not know spring and autumn. However, in the endless torrent of time, ten thousand years is only like a hundred steps compared to fifty steps, because sooner or later everyone will die!

Now is the era of the Republic, and Emperor Xuantong's [queue sovereignty] has already kicked the bucket. Smart people then, based on the principle of [Chinese learning for the essence, Western learning for practical use], re-translated the two characters [Long Live] from foreign languages and applied them everywhere. People not only do not find these two characters feudal and annoying, but consider them fresh and fashionable. This can probably echo the two characters [Revolution], which have been turned from old to new one after the other. But the ultimate meaning of [Long Live] always has a bit of a somber taste.

Westerners are indeed much smarter than us. They do not use finite numbers as congratulatory terms, so they do not feel that there is still a [taste of death] in the end. For example, the British shout [Long live the King!]. The French shout [Vive la Republique! (Long live the Republic)]. The German royalists enthusiastically shout [Es lebe der Konig! (Long live the German Emperor)]. Soviet workers fervently shout [Da Zdrevstvuet Proletarskaya Revolyutsiya (Long live the proletarian revolution)]. According to the original meaning of words such as Long live, vive, etc., they are all congratulating something or other on living or living long. Compared to the Chinese shouting of something or other [ten thousand years], they do not feel a chill. Therefore, although the translation of the two characters [Long Live] is skillfully done, it is somewhat of an ancient person's mistake, from which the difficulty of translation can also be seen!

The short Easterners are even worse than us. Like parrots learning to speak, they stole the essence of Chinese culture [Long Live] and silently turned Wansai into the voiced Banzai. Last year, thousands of Korean children waved the sun flag in Hongkou and shouted Banzai Tennobaai (Long live the Emperor) to the new Japanese reinforcements arriving in Shanghai. Thinking of it now, I still sigh at the fact that the short ones are incorrigible. But these short ones not only shout [Long Live the Emperor] themselves in a dull-witted way, but are now frantically forcing others to bark along with them. Didn't famous traitors such as Yu Chonghan and Xie Jieshi lead a group of [Manchukuo] beauties and handsome men to Tokyo last year, shouting Fenno Banzai? I don't know what the traitors will call the young Xuantong, but if the restoration is successful, they will probably only be able to give him a nauseating [Thousand Years] at most.

Finally, let me bring the topic back to the beginning. Although I personally feel that [Long Live] is a bit unlucky, we will temporarily continue to use the two characters [Long Live] until there is a suitable word to translate [Long live...]. However, we do not hope that those who use the bones of the common people to make their thrones will [Long Live]; but we hope and pray that the systems and ideas that represent justice and truth will [Long Live]! Ten thousand years, ten thousand years, to infinity. Let the two characters [Long Live] also [Long Live] forever: [Long Live] Long Live!

Swearing 227

— Gan

"May Heaven punish me and the earth destroy me, may I be a male thief and a female prostitute" – this is the classic Chinese oath, almost like "The Book of Poetry says," "Confucius said." Today's oaths, "[swear to kill the enemy, swear to resist to the death, swear...]" seem to not use these kinds of idioms.

But the substance of swearing is still the same, which is that you can't trust it. They know full well that Heaven is not necessarily going to punish them, and the earth is not necessarily going to destroy them. Nowadays, even ginseng is [scientifically made] by including electricity, so how can [Heaven and Earth] not be scientific! As for male thieves and female prostitutes, that is not only harmless but also beneficial; male thieves can acquire several more layers of land, and female prostitutes can get a few more positions for [relatives of officials].

My old friend said: Your explanations of [thief] and [prostitute] are not the ancient meanings. I said - you know what era this is! This is an era where thieves are modern, and prostitutes are modern, so swearing is also modern, and has turned into oaths.

Random Words from Qu Lu (Two) 228

— Zizhan

Even Ghosts Advocate for Vernacular Chinese

Dr. Hu Mingfu was the most promising scientist in our country, but unfortunately, he died by drowning on June 13, 1927. The Science Society of China held a special social funeral for him. Mr. Yang Xingfo's epitaph for Hu Mingfu reads: [Knowledge is boundless, but life is finite, I wish to burn myself to create the light of mankind. While the world is drunk on wealth and honor, Mr. is dedicated to the unknown. When strength is exhausted, the heart is at peace, death and success are not worth discussing. The river flows endlessly, and the mountain colors are eternally green. For thousands and ten thousands of years, protect this good city forever. For thousands and ten thousands of years, protect this good city forever.] If the dead really have knowledge, they may not approve of such clichés and stock phrases. But to say the dead have no knowledge? They can actually give oracles and advocate for vernacular Chinese. Ms. Hu Binxia's brief biography of her late brother, Mingfu, states: [During spirit writing, I asked whether this piece should be written in classical or vernacular Chinese, and he replied vernacular, so I followed his advice.] Since the deceased was a scientist, and this article is published in a science magazine, as if spirit writing truly has ghostly possession, is it not a great strange thing? Even ghosts advocate for vernacular Chinese; I will send this message to Hu Shi.

Four Hu Yunyi's Hao Lu Teacher

One day, my friend Wu Qiren asked me if Hu Yunyi's Hao Lu teacher was Huang Pei? I stared blankly, not knowing how to answer. Mr. Wu immediately took Hu's book "Research on Song Ci" from the bookshelf and showed it to me, page 166, the entry on the lyricist Jiang Baishi, where it was seen that the author quoted [Hao Lu Teacher saying: The presence of Baishi in lyric poetry is like the presence of Changli in prose.] I said; [This is probably Xu Hao Lu of the prosperous Qing Dynasty, the Hao Lu teacher who was often praised by Zhang Yongchuan, the author of Cilin Jishi.] Mr. Wu then took out Cilin Jishi and checked the Jiang Kui entry, and indeed saw a small note quoting [Hao Lu Teacher saying; The presence of Baishi in lyric poetry is like the presence of Changli in prose. It is also fitting that the world regards those who consider Changli to be contrived and awkward also consider Baishi to be stiff.] Mr. Wu laughed and said; [Fortunately, I am contemporary with Mr. Hu. If Mr. Hu had been born one hundred and forty to fifty years earlier, I would have believed that Xu Hao Lu had gained another highly talented disciple besides Zhang Zongpu.] Mr. Wu has authored research on "Rou Pu Tuan" and also authored a defense that Confucius was not born from an improper union, in order to correct the errors of past commentators of Shiji, making him a person with both a historical obsession and an obsession with textual research.

The Era of Long Creative Works and the Crossroads of Love (Continued) Zhang Ping 229

"It's really annoying! You know I live in Fort Taiwan. Because there is a one-hour class at H Liang College today, scheduled from eight to nine. But in your school, classes are only in the afternoon at three o'clock. Once I come out, I have to go back and come out again, which not only costs more money for transportation but also wastes time. So after class at the Japan Academy, I have no choice but to go to your school's library to kill this half-day. Shanghai's professor life is really not a human life! ... Last night I prepared several courses and went to bed after twelve o'clock. After lying down in bed, I became restless and couldn't sleep. I tossed and turned until two or three o'clock before falling asleep. Today I have a terrible headache, a terrible headache!"

As Mr. Zhu spoke of having a terrible headache, he twitched his nose, bit his molars, and knitted his brows. "Just one hour at H College? Wouldn't it be better to not take the job? This way, it's too hard on you, isn't it?"

Haiquan couldn't help but feel sympathetic when he heard Mr. Zhu complaining.

"No. There are three classes, but the times can't be arranged on the same day. I have to go on two separate days, two o'clock on Monday, and noon today...."

"How much per hour?"

"H College is the most economical, two yuan, eight jiao, and five fen."

"That's not much. Wouldn't it be better to quit?"

"...................................................................."

Mr. Zhu smiled bitterly and sighed deeply, as if hating that Haiquan had no understanding of the professors' suffering, and was speechless for a moment. But after a while, Mr. Zhu smiled again and said:

"Three twos are six, three eights are twenty-four, three fives are fifteen, a total of eight yuan, five jiao, and five fen. Excluding transportation costs, at least if I don't take leave every week, I can simply earn seven yuan and five jiao more, which is not a small supplement, not a small supplement."

Talking Points

China Will Not Perish 230

— Wu

Recently, people have often predicted that China will inevitably perish, and even in my opinion, it seems very possible. This, of course, refers to perishing in the kowtows and obeisances of some important figures, and will certainly not simply fade away without any incident. However, in the past few days, I have become a bit doubtful; I feel that China may not necessarily perish, and you never know. Haven't even the sister-in-law of the Manchurian emperor become patriotic?

According to reports, the puppet Puyi's sister-in-law, Pu Tang Shixia, is willing to reconcile with her husband, Pu Jie, because: [Since he (Jie) went to Japan for studies, for several years, Xia has been trapped in Beiping, and eunuch servants have deliberately provoked discord. The family patriarch listened to slanderous words and often heard things that made Xia unable to feel at ease.] Moreover, [When Puyi was taken east by the Japanese, he had tearfully pleaded with the family patriarch beforehand, but the family patriarch instead criticized Xia for being nosy,] so this female hero who deeply understands righteousness [had no choice but to leave the mansion alone, preferring to be a lonely soul of China rather than be a relative of the puppet emperor, and therefore going to Changchun was absolutely impossible]. However, it is not completely without room for turning around, as it says later: [If my husband cherishes the love of our married life and comes to Shanghai to be with Xia, Xia will advocate on his behalf to those in power, and it will not be difficult for him to have a foothold. Otherwise, if he fails temporarily, he will be discredited along with his colleagues, leaving behind the condemnation of posterity, and there will be no place for him to stand at home or abroad.]

Judging from this great principle, that she does not go to the Northeast is of course because she [prefers to be a lonely soul of China rather than be a relative of the puppet emperor,] not to mention that this woman is commendable. Just from these two sentences, we are worthy of erecting a stone memorial arch for her to spread her benevolence to ten thousand ages and thousands of autumns, not to mention that when Puyi went east, she had tearfully pleaded with him, so it is even more commendable and worthy of tears. In addition, the bitter rain and cold wind of being trapped in Beiping for several years, this situation and this scene, can be imagined. However, there is still the love of married life. If that person can come to Shanghai and be with her, she will still not hesitate to advocate on his behalf to those in power. This part, of course, will not be bragging, as the public officials in charge of reason will naturally not find it difficult to turn around and make arrangements for him. Therefore, both loving the country and reuniting, the beautiful things in the world, there should be nothing better than this. However, upon further thought, the so-called [leaving behind the condemnation of posterity] part, Ms. Tang need not worry too much about. Who cares about the affairs of posterity? Moreover, this has the same effect as [leaving a fragrant name for a thousand years], is it not also praised by people in the same way? Moreover, relatives of the puppet emperor are, after all, hard to come by. How many lives can one have? Why not fully savor the taste of it?

However, all said and done, the foundation of China is still reliable, because even our imperial relatives have surprisingly become patriotic.

A Glimpse Outside the Window 231

— Ms. Bingqing

On an afternoon after a rainy day, I led our newly hired servant to my alma mater to pick up my younger brother.

I silently dragged a pair of heavy, broken cotton boots, looking down at the muddy street, picking out the drier spots to step on. In my heart, I only felt that the boots were too heavy and clumsy.

Turning a corner, I could already see that majestic and towering alma mater in the distance. I turned my head back and said to him, [Do you see it?] [That's it.]

It was still early, and there were still thirty minutes before school was dismissed. I was impatient to wait, so I only led him to my brother's classroom and instructed him to [be careful on the road], and then I hurriedly left. When passing by the doorway of the teachers' room for the middle and high grade levels, I sneakily walked closer and peeked into the window. Although I wasn't looking for Mr. Jiang [my former homeroom teacher] to talk, I really wanted to see his respected face. I felt that Mr. Jiang's kind of rigorous and peaceful attitude was unmatched by anyone else.

In that row by the window, the window of the last seat let in a dim light. It seemed unwilling to shine on other teachers, only shining on the shoulder of a female teacher wearing black clothes. Who else could this upright and noble teacher be but Mr. Jiang? I didn't want to go in and interrupt the valuable time that he was enthusiastically putting his spirit into correcting students' papers.

In this glimpse outside the window, indescribable sweet, sour, bitter, and spicy flavors welled up in my heart. I seemed to want to laugh, and I seemed to want to cry. How could I, who is barely literate, describe this moment that is difficult to speak of?

I only felt that I was not blessed enough to receive the guidance of this motherly teacher. In this glimpse, I seemed to see a great man of the world. When I came out, I only felt honored and happy.
